<P_I,313>

{ED:1._CROMWELL_TO_JOHN_CREKE.}

{ED:Aug._17_[1523].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Maister Creke as hertelye as I can I commende me CROMWEL,I,313.001.1

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and in the same wise thanke yow <em> for your </em> gentill and louyng
letteres to me at sundrye tymys Sent CROMWEL,I,313.001.2

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and wher as I accordinglye haue not in lyke wise remembrid and
rescribid it hath bene for that I haue not hade anything to wryt of to
your aduauncement . Whom I assure yow yf it were in my lytyll power I
coulde be well contentyd to preferre as ferre as any one man lyuyng .
CROMWEL,I,313.001.3

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But at this present I being at Sum layser entending to remembre and
also remunerate the olde acquayntaunces and to renew our not forgoten
Sundrye communycacions Supposing ye desyre to know the newes curraunt
in thes partyes CROMWEL,I,313.001.4

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
for it is said that newes refresshith the $spyrit of lyffe , wherfor ye
shall vnderstonde that by long tyme I amongist other haue Indured a
parlyament which contenwid by the space of xvij hole wekes wher we
communyd of warre pease Stryffe contencyon debatte murmure grudge
Riches pouerte penurye trowth falshode Justyce equyte discayte
opprescyon Magnanymyte actyuyte force attempraunce Treason murder
Felonye consyli ... and also how a commune welth myght be ediffyed and
$also contenewid within our Realme . CROMWEL,I,313.001.5

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Howbeyt in conclusyon we haue $done as our predecessors haue been wont
to doo that ys to say , as well as we myght and lefte wher we begann .
CROMWEL,I,313.001.6

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
ye shall also vnderstond the Duke of Suthffolke Furnysshyd with a gret
armye goyth ouer in all goodlye hast $whither I know not ,
CROMWEL,I,313.001.7

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
when I know I shall aduertyse yow . CROMWEL,I,313.001.8

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Whe haue in our parlyament grauntyd vnto the Kinges highnes a right
large Subsydye , the lyke wherof was neuer grauntyd in this realme .
CROMWEL,I,313.001.9

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
all your frendes to my knowlage be in good helth and specially thay
that ye wott of : CROMWEL,I,313.001.10

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
ye know what I meane . CROMWEL,I,313.001.11

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I thinke it best to wryt in parables $because I am In dowt .
CROMWEL,I,313.001.12

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Maister Vawhan Fareth well CROMWEL,I,313.001.13

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:38?
RECIPIENT:JOHN_CREKE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_001:E1:1523:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and so doth Maister $Munkcaster . CROMWEL,I,313.001.14

<P_I,314>

{ED:2._CROMWELL_TO_ELIZABETH_HIS_WIFE.}

{ED:Nov._29_[1525].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?
RECIPIENT:ELIZABETH_CROMWELL[N.WYKYS]:FEMALE:WIFE:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_002:E1:1525:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Elyzabeth I commend me unto you CROMWEL,I,314.002.21

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?
RECIPIENT:ELIZABETH_CROMWELL[N.WYKYS]:FEMALE:WIFE:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_002:E1:1525:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and have sente you by this berer a fatt doo , the one half whereof I
pray you may be delyvered unto my gossyp mastres Smyth , and with the
rest to use your pleasure . CROMWEL,I,314.002.22

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?
RECIPIENT:ELIZABETH_CROMWELL[N.WYKYS]:FEMALE:WIFE:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_002:E1:1525:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And further yf Richard Swifte be cum home or fortune to cum shortly , I
will that he resorte to me at Begham or Tonbridge with all dylygence .
CROMWEL,I,314.002.23

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?
RECIPIENT:ELIZABETH_CROMWELL[N.WYKYS]:FEMALE:WIFE:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_002:E1:1525:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Such news as ye have in those partyes I pray you sende me parte by this
berer . CROMWEL,I,314.002.24

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?
RECIPIENT:ELIZABETH_CROMWELL[N.WYKYS]:FEMALE:WIFE:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_002:E1:1525:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
At Begham the xxix=th= day of November . CROMWEL,I,314.002.25

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?
RECIPIENT:ELIZABETH_CROMWELL[N.WYKYS]:FEMALE:WIFE:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_002:E1:1525:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And farther I pray you sende me word in wryting who hathe resorted unto
you syns my departuer from you to speke with me . CROMWEL,I,314.002.26

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:40?

<Q_CRO_A_1528_T_TCROMWELL> <L_CROMWEL_003> <A_THOMAS_CROMWELL>
<A-GENDER_MALE> <A-REL_---> <A-DOB_1485?> <R_THOMAS_WOLSEY>
<R-GENDER_MALE> <R-REL_---> <R-DOB_1473?>

<P_I,318>

{ED:6._CROMWELL_TO_WOLSEY.}

{ED:April_2,_1528.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please it your grace to be aduertised how that I according to your most
gracyous commaundement haue repayred vnto the late monasterye of
Wallingforde Where I founde aswell all the ornamenttes of the churche
as all other ymplementtes of houseolde clerely conueyed awaye and
nothing remayning . Sauyng only the euydences Which I sorted and
conueyed vnto your colledge at Oxforde And the same delyvered vnto your
Dean there . CROMWEL,I,318.003.29

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And afterwardes Mr. Croke and I surueyed amended and refourmed aswell
the letteres patentes graunted by the king his highnes vnto your grace
as also your gyftes and graunttes made vnto your said colledge in suche
wise I trust that no defaulte or omyssyon at this tyme is lefte
vnrefourmed . CROMWEL,I,318.003.30

<P_I,319>

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I haue also founde offyces aswell of the saide late monasterye of
Wallingforde and of all the londes and tenementtes belonging to the
same within the Counties of Oxforde and Berk as also of suche omyssions
as were omytted within the saide counties belonging to Frediswides and
Lytlemore . CROMWEL,I,319.003.31

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And now I do repayre into the Counties of Buck and Bedforde for offyces
to be founde there aswell of suche londes as apperteyne to the saide
late monasterye of Wallingforde as also to the late monasterye of Praye
besides saincte Albons . CROMWEL,I,319.003.32

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The buyldinges of your noble colledge most prosperouslye and
magnyfycently dothe arryse in suche wise that to euery mannes iudgement
the lyke thereof was neuer sene ne ymagened hauing consideracyon to the
largeness beautee sumptuous Curyous and most substauncyall buylding of
the same . CROMWEL,I,319.003.33

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your chapell within the saide colledge most deuoutely and vertuously
ordered CROMWEL,I,319.003.34

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And the mynistres within the same not onely dyligent in the seruyce of
god but also the seruice daylie doon within the same so deuoute
solempne and full of Armonye that in myne opynyon it hathe fewe peres .
CROMWEL,I,319.003.35

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
There is a benefyce voyde within the dyoces of saincte dauyes in Wales
which is of your gracyous gyfte by meane of the chauncelorship of
Englonde . CROMWEL,I,319.003.36

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Yf it may please your grace to gyue the same to Mr. Byrton he shoulde
be the more able to do your grace seruyce . CROMWEL,I,319.003.37

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The name of the saide benefyce is called sayncte Florence .
CROMWEL,I,319.003.38

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I assure your grace the saide Mr. Byrton is a right honest man And by
somme reporte right well lerned and shall do your grace good seruyce .
CROMWEL,I,319.003.39

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My besyness accomplisshed I shall according to my duetie repayre vnto
your grace . CROMWEL,I,319.003.40

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Most humblye beseching the holie trynytee contynuallye to preserue the
prosperous astate of the same in long lif and good helth .
CROMWEL,I,319.003.41

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
At Oxforde the Seconde day of Aprell . CROMWEL,I,319.003.42

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_003:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your most humble seruaunt Thomas Crumwell . CROMWEL,I,319.003.43

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?

<P_I,321>

{ED:8._CROMWELL_TO_WOLSEY.}

{ED:[Sept._3,_1528.]}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please it your grace to haue in remembraunce your Fynours of Duresme
whose contynuaunce here is not onely to their greate cost and losse of
tyme but also to the greate hinderaunce of your werkes ther ,
CROMWEL,I,321.004.45

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and also they be veray poore , CROMWEL,I,321.004.46

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
your gracious pleasure therfore wold be knowen whether they shall
resorte to your presence , or howe otherwise your grace will they
$shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} ordred CROMWEL,I,321.004.47

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I haue according to your moste gracious commaundement sent herein
inclosed the clere yerely valeurs of all suche londes as ye haue
purchased in the Counties of Yorke and Buckingham , and also the clere
yerely value of the late monasterie of Wallingforde
CROMWEL,I,321.004.48

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
If it may stonde with your pleasure to appoynte in whose name your
grace intendithe to dedicate your colledge in <P_I,322> Gipswiche , and
by what name the maister and fellowes $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} called ,
the lycence of erexion , the letteres patenttes , pryuate Seales and
other thinges necessarie for the same myght be put in a redynes
CROMWEL,I,322.004.49

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
so that no tyme shulde be loste I haue caused suche billes as be
allredie signed to passe the pryuy signet and pryuate Seale ,
CROMWEL,I,322.004.50

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and shall nowe put to wryting the letteres patenttes for the brode
Seale , so that after the iii monethes expired your grace may geue the
londes conteyned within the same according to youre moste gracious
pleasure . CROMWEL,I,322.004.51

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
It $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} well done that your grace haue in
remembraunce thappropriacion of the benefices to your colledge in
Oxford , and that an ende maye be takyn withe all ordynaries which I
thinke is not yet done CROMWEL,I,322.004.52

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I haue spoken with maister Babington nowe lorde of Kylmayne for the
exchaunge to be made bitwene your colledge in Oxforde and his religion
for Saundforde , CROMWEL,I,322.004.53

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
It may therfore please your grace that your pleasure may be knowen
whether this vacacion your counsaile shall farther commune withe hym
and other whiche haue auctoritie in that behalf , or not , whiche in
myn opynyon shulde be well done , and will sett your purpose in a great
forwardnes CROMWEL,I,322.004.54

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
It may also please your grace that these instruccions herein inclosed
may be sent to maister Holgill for thordering of hymself in taking
possession lyueraye and season at Rudby , whiche Instruccions were
deuysed by the Judges , CROMWEL,I,322.004.55

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and it $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} necessarie that he haue them withe
spede . CROMWEL,I,322.004.56

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:55?
LETTER:CROMWEL_004:E1:1528:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your gracious pleasure knowen touching the premisses I shall most
humblie indeuoir myself according to my duetie to accomplisshe your
most gracious commaundement , As knowithe the holly trynytie vnto whome
I shall daily during my lyfe praye for the prosperous conseruacion of
your good grace CROMWEL,I,322.004.57

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:43?

{ED:9._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:Jan._18_[1529].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:44?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:32?
LETTER:CROMWEL_005:E1:1529:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Worshipfull Sir , after most hartie comendacyons it may please you to
aduertise my lorde his grace that the cause Why I do not repayre
thither at this present ys for that I haue certen bokes to be don and
accomplisshed concerning his colledge in Gipswich That is to say a
deade of gyfte from his grace to his saide colledge of the late
monasteryes of Felixstowe Rumburgh and Bromehill The King his letteres
patentes of assent to the Suppression of the same late monasteryes ,
The King his letteres patentes of assent to the pope his bull of
exempcyon of the saide colledge The King his letteres patentes of
lycence for thimpropryacion of the benefyces belongyng to the saide
late monasteryes A deade of gyft from the Duke of Norff. to my lord his
grace of the saide late monasterye of Felixstowe A relesse from the
prior <P_I,324> and conuent of Rochester of all theyr right tytle and
patronage of in or to the same late pryory of Felixstowe A relesse from
the abbot and conuent of Saynct Maryes in Yorke of all their right and
tytle in or to the late pryory of Rumburgh A relesse from my lorde of
Oxforde of all his right and tytle in the late pryory of Bromehill And
a relesse from the Frenssh quene and the duke of Suffolk of all theyr
right and tytle in the manours of Sayes courte and Byckeling and in the
late pryorye of Snape . All which bokes be not yet in a redynes ne
parfyted vnto my mynde Intending assone as the same $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} fynysshed and made parfyte , whiche I trust $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} to morow at nyght or wenesday by none at the Ferthest to
repayre vnto my lorde his grace , vppon his gracyous pleasure knowen
for thinsealing of the same CROMWEL,I,324.005.65

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:44?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:32?
LETTER:CROMWEL_005:E1:1529:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
accordingly It may also please you to aduertise my lorde his grace that
Sythen his repayree to Rychmond I have ben at Lyesnes Where I saw one
of the most pyteous and greuous sightes that ever I saw which to me
before the Sight of the same was incredyble concernyng the breche out
of the Thamyse into the marsshes of Lyesnes which be all ouerflowen and
drowned And that at the last chaunge the tyde was so high that there
happened a new breche which hathe fordone asmoche worke there as will
cost ccc=li= the new making of the same In so moche that if my being
there had not ben to haue incouraged the workemen and labourers I
assure you all the labour and money that hathe ben ther spent
heretofore had ben clerely lost and cast away . And the workemen and
labourers wolde haue departed and left all at chaunce whiche shoulde
haue ben the gretest yuell that euer happened to the countrey ther .
CROMWEL,I,324.005.66

bothe be content that your gift shall stande so as your grace do
accomplishe the tenour of his hieghnes Letteres nowe eftsones directed
vnto youe , whiche myn advise and counsail is that youe shall in any
wise ensue , and that your chauncelour shall do the semblable <P_I,329>

graceous remembraunce how that I being with your grace in your gallerie
at the Chartrehouse at Shene most humblie supplied vnto the same for
the acceptacion of this berer Mr. doctour Carbot my kynsman vnto your
seruice At which tyme it pleased your grace beninglie to graunt me to
accept hym promising both-5 vnto him and me that ye wolde be his good
and graceous Lorde vpon the which he hath tarried here in these parties
Contynuallye to his great cost Supposing that I sholde haue repared
with him vnto your grace by meane wherof he thought the better to be
esteemed CROMWEL,I,330.008.93

dilligent and honest And suchon that Willinglie Louinglie and
obedientlie shall and $wil $be {TEXT:wilbe} gladde to serue your grace
in any thing that your pleaser $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} to commaunde

humble sute and contemplacion to take him withowt reiection

{ED:18._[CROMWELL]_TO_WOLSEY.}

{ED:August_18_[1530].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:45?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:57?
LETTER:CROMWEL_009:E1:1530:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please it your grace to be aduertised that after the Receipt of your
letteres dated at Southwell on saynt Laurence Day I perceyued how that
your grace remayned in som displeasure and anxietie of mynde for that I
by my letteres had before certefied you of the fynding certen offices
concerning your busshopriche of Yorke The Fynding whereof as I perceyue
by your letteres ye do suppose should be moche to your dishonour &
detriment For the which intent that your grace may put yourself in
repose & quietacion of mynde I haue sent vnto you this berer who shall
at length declare vnto you besides the demonstracion of the copies of
suche offices as be drawen for that purpose that the Fynding of the
said offices savyng onelie that in the preamble of the same there is
touched the conuiction of your grace in the premunire which all the
wourld alredie knoweth $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} for your good onelie
proffit and availe CROMWEL,I,331.009.99

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:45?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:57?
LETTER:CROMWEL_009:E1:1530:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And yet your pardon and restitucion stand in good & perfite effecte So
that your grace shal haue no nede nether to be in fere of losse of any
your spirituall or temporall goodes or to be troubeled for the same ne
also to be put to any new Sute in the obteyning of any other pardon or
restitucion . CROMWEL,I,331.009.100

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:45?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:57?
LETTER:CROMWEL_009:E1:1530:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And if in case your said pardon and restitucion were in any parte
insufficient I assure your grace I know that the kinges highnes wold it
should be made as good as by any counsaill it could be Devised
CROMWEL,I,331.009.101

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:45?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WOLSEY:MALE:_:1473?:57?
LETTER:CROMWEL_009:E1:1530:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And doubt ye not but his highnes is your gracyous and benigne
Souereigne lorde and wold in no wise that ye should be greued molested
or troubeled . Wherfore it may please your grace to quiet yourself and
to take the fynding of these offices pacientlie CROMWEL,I,331.009.102

Instruccions Beseching you to Survey the same and if ye shall fynde any
erroure to order and correcte hit according to your wysdomme and
goodnes or euer ye shall presente the sight thereof vnto the Kinges
highnes which ons donne and his highe pleasure knowne I shall with
dylygence cause it to be engrossed and sent CROMWEL,I,340.010.139

long loked and wisshed for As our lorde knoweth etc .

commawndment to me youyn yesterdaye haue Inclosyd them in this my
lettere , wherby your highnes shall and may woll persayue of what
Importaunce they be of . CROMWEL,I,344.012.152

weight but that he wrytythe that your gracyous ambasadours do now
repayre to the emperours ambassadours to Dunkyrke affermyng them to be
Suffycyentlye Furnysshyd to answer all thinges layd by the contrarye
parte and nothing dowtyth but that they shall haue veray gud Successe
in all your gracyous affayres CROMWEL,I,344.012.153

{ED:36._[CROMWELL]_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:[September,_1532.]}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:47?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:41

commaundement I haue caused patrons to be drawen after your graces

of any thing In perffeccyon vntill your gracious pleasure $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} Ferther knowen for the which purpose both he and I shall
repayre vnto your highnes on Saterday night or Sondaye in the morning
CROMWEL,I,348.014.161

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:47?

LETTER:CROMWEL_014:E1:1532:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
touching a certen matier in varyaunce betwixt thexecutours of Sir
William Spencer disceasyd and my ladye spencer whereas informacion was
made vnto your highnes that grete Spoyle of the goodes of the saide Sir
William Spencer was made by the saide executours and how that the
executours wold haue put owt my ladye late the wyff of the sayd William
from the execucyon of the testament the matier hath ben harde here
before my lorde the keper of your grete seale Sir Willyam Poulet and me
. CROMWEL,I,348.014.163

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:47?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:41
LETTER:CROMWEL_014:E1:1532:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as it appereth by thexamynacion as well of the executors as by
Edmond Knyghtley and Rychard his brother the hole spoyle and eloyning
of the sayd goods & plate was made onely by the sayd Edmond Knyghtley
his brother Rychard and the sayd ladye spencer thayr suster
notwithstanding that ther was Agrement made betwene the executors and
the ladye spencer that she sholde entyr into bargayn with your highnes
and also into the execucyon of the testament with them as an executrix
which vndowtydly she hadde done yf Edmond Knyghtle hadde not bene Which
Edmonde Knightley <P_I,349> hathe not onelie trauayled asmoche as in
him is to sett pyke betwene the sayd ladye and the executors and to
defeate your grace of your title to the heire of the saide Spencer but
also Justeffyed the same befor my sayd lorde keper of the gret Seale
wher on the other partye it was openlye prouyd that your grace hade
good tytyll and all his allegacyon vntrew CROMWEL,I,349.014.164

yet neuertheles for the reducing of the same his vntrew purpose to

Warwyke leycester & Northampton in dyuers of your highnes Towns there
to the high contempte of your grace and your lawes
CROMWEL,I,349.014.165

ayenst your highnes in that behalf my lorde the keper of your grete

{ED:57._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE}

{ED:Sept._21_[1533].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_017:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Aftre my right harty Commendacions to your lordshipp Whereas heretofore
I addressed my letteres vnto your lordshipp at the sute of my seruaunt
Bartholomew Bayneham concernyng the steye of such goodes as lately
apperteyned to his Father Robert Baynam of Calaish vntil suche tyme as
ye harde Further of my mynde in that behaulf . These $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} most hertely to desyer and praye youe the rather at the
contemplacion hereof to suffre thexecutours of his sayd Father Robert
Baynam to execute and mynistre according to the meanyng of the
Testament and last wyll of his sayd Father in as ample wise as {in}_P
heretofore they haue doon my sayd former letteres notwithstanding .
CROMWEL,I,365.017.197

vnto my sayd seruaunt partely as I take yt for my sake I thanke you
most hertely for the same CROMWEL,I,365.017.198

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?

youe doo presently extende Vnto him . Wherein ye shall admynystre Vnto
me Veray acceptable pleasur . CROMWEL,I,365.017.199

<P_I,367>

{ED:60._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:Nov._11_[1533].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My lorde after my right hertie commendacions I haue receyued your
lordeshippes letteres CROMWEL,I,367.018.204

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And haue perceyued by the same what contencion is arrysen there by
meanes of a lewde Felowe for a stroke yeven vnto him by Sir Cristofer
Garnysshe the knight porter , Which matier hath ben debated here by the
kinges counsaile who perceyuing the saide stroke was yeven but onelie
for correction and for none entente to breke any law statute or
ordenaunce of that towne of Calays , do thinke the same but a veray
light matier to make any suche busynes of and no cause why the saide
Sir Cristofer should be put to any molestacion for the same . Wherefore
your lordeship may let it passe and wey it as it is
CROMWEL,I,367.018.205

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And so our lorde preserue your lordeship in long lif and helth with
moche honour CROMWEL,I,367.018.206

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
At London the xi day of Nouember . CROMWEL,I,367.018.207

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
$I do also hertelie thanke your lordsship for your grete chere made to
my seruaunte $Willyam Johnson and to this gentilman straungier for whom
I do wryte vnto your lordeship at this tyme by myn other letteres .
CROMWEL,I,367.018.208

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And for all other your lordshippes gentilnes I do most hertelie thanke
you trusting if I lyue to requyte the same if I can .
CROMWEL,I,367.018.209

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your lordshyppis assuryd Freend Thomas Crumwell . CROMWEL,I,367.018.210

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_018:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
{ED:ADD.} To the right honourable and his singuler good lorde the lorde
vicount Lisle deputie to the kinges highnes of his towne and marcheis
of Calays . CROMWEL,I,367.018.211

{ED:65._[CROMWELL]_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:1533.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Pleasyth it your Royall magestye to be aduertysyd how that reparyng
homwardes oone of my lorde chauncelers <P_I,371> seruaunttes met with
me and delyuerid me your warraunttes Signyd with the hande of the
prynces dowager which warrauntt I do send to your grace herin Inclosyd
CROMWEL,I,371.019.212

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
what your plesure $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} to haue done therin being
ons known I shall right gladlye accomplyshe CROMWEL,I,371.019.213

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I haue also Sythyn my repayre to london spokyn with Freer Lawraunce who
hathe Sethens his Repayre to london herde dyuers thinges touching the
holye mayde which he wyll declare to your hygnes and to non other
CROMWEL,I,371.019.214

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and he Shewyth me also that {TEXT:that} ther be ij=o= strange Freers of
the order of obseruanttes latelye repayryd into this Realme which ij=o=
Freers haue exploryd here For all suche bokes centencys and
determynacyons as hathe passyd touching your hygnes Matrymonye , which
they Intend with other pryvey practysys to Convey with them , to Freer
Petow who as I am Credyblye Informyd Sent them into this your Realme
CROMWEL,I,371.019.215

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
the sayd ij=o= Freers as I am acertaynyd haue browght with them pryuy
letteres to dyuers CROMWEL,I,371.019.216

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and now bene gone to the sayd dowager . CROMWEL,I,371.019.217

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
in my poore oppynyon it $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} right well done that
thaye might be sent For by Some trustye person CROMWEL,I,371.019.218

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
howbeit yt were best that theye Fyrste sholde be sufferyd to speke with
her and suche other of hers as woolde peraduenture delyuer to them
anything wherby theyr Ferther practysys myght be persayuyd
CROMWEL,I,371.019.219

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and so thayr Cankeryd Intenttes myght be therbye dyscyfferyd .
CROMWEL,I,371.019.220

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I am also Infformyd that there ys A merchant of london whiche dothe
practyse with them in thes premysses CROMWEL,I,371.019.221

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I shall goo veray nere to haue knowlage therein CROMWEL,I,371.019.222

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
yf it be trew he ys worthye to Suffer to make other beware in tyme he
ys of good Substaunce . CROMWEL,I,371.019.223

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?

I trust your highnes wyll by this berer aduertyse me in wrytyng what

CROMWEL,I,371.019.227

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:48?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:42
LETTER:CROMWEL_019:E1:1533:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I haue also Sent to your grace one acquytance to be assigned for the
xxiiij=ti= thousande Crowns dew to your highnes for the resedew of the

CROMWEL,I,372.019.230

<P_I,373>

{ED:67._[CROMWELL]_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:January_[1534].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:43
LETTER:CROMWEL_020:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
$Pleasyth $yt {TEXT:Pleasythyt} your most Royall Mageste to be
aduertysyd how that according to your most highe pleasure and
commaundement I haue made serche for suche patenttes and grauntys as
your highnes and also the most Famous kyng your father whos Sowle our
lorde pardon haue grauntyd vnto sir Rychard Weston knyght your
vndertesawrer of your exchequer and the same haue sent to your highnes
herin closyd CROMWEL,I,373.020.231

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:43
LETTER:CROMWEL_020:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
yt may also please your most Royall Mageste to knowe how that
yesterdaye ther passyd your Commons a byll that no person within this
your Realme shall herafter kepe and Noryshe aboue the Nombre of twoo
thousand shepe and also that the eight parte of euerye mans lande being
a Fermour shall for euer herafter be put in tyllage yerlye which byll
yf by the gret wysdom vertuew goodnes and zerale that your highnes
beryth towardes this your Realme might haue good Successe and take good
effect Amongyst your lordes aboue I doo Coniecture and Suppose in my
pore Symple and vnworthye Judgement that your highnes shall do the most
noble proffyttable and most benefycyall thing that euer was done to the
Commone welthe of this your Realme and shall therby Increase suche
welthe in the same amongyst the gret Nombre & multytude for your most
louyng and $obedyent Subiectys as neuer was Seane in this Realme Sythen
Brewtyse tyme CROMWEL,I,373.020.232

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:43
LETTER:CROMWEL_020:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
most humblye prostrate at the Fete of your Magnifycence beseche your
highnes to pardon my boldnes $in this wrytyng to your grace which onlye
procedythe for the trowthe dewtye allegaunce and loue I doo bere to
your mageste and the Common welth of this your Realme as our lorde
knowyth vnto whom I shall as I am most bounden Incessantlye praye for
the contenewans & prosperous conseruacyon of your most excellent most
Royall and Imperyall estate long to Indure CROMWEL,I,373.020.233

<P_I,380>

{ED:70._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:Apr._24_[1534].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:37?
LETTER:CROMWEL_021:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My Lord in my right hertie wise I commende me to you .
CROMWEL,I,380.021.234

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:37?
LETTER:CROMWEL_021:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as I haue been , and wolbe glad and redy , to do you suche pleasire
as I myght or may . so I desire you to graunt vnto me to the behoue of
a dere frende of myne . the aduocation of the parsonaige of S. Jhons of
$Shireborne in hampshire being of your gift . whiche is of the yerely
value of x or $xj $=li= {TEXT:xj=li=} and not aboue <paren> as I am
informed </paren> by the gyft whereof ye shal shewe vnto me a right
acceptable pleasire . whiche I wol not forgete when I may in recompense
thereof . do the thing that may be to your contentation .
CROMWEL,I,380.021.235

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:37?
LETTER:CROMWEL_021:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And of your beniuolent mynd in this behalf , I desire you not only to
certifie me by your next writing but also to direct your letters to
your vicar generall and to the priour and conuent of your churche . for
thexpedition thereof to be made in due forme , and to be deliuered vnto
me with suche spede as shall pleace you to commaunde thaim .
CROMWEL,I,380.021.236

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:37?
LETTER:CROMWEL_021:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
the xxiiij=th= day of Aprile . CROMWEL,I,380.021.237

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:37?
LETTER:CROMWEL_021:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your lordshippis assuryd freeind Thomas Crumwell .
CROMWEL,I,380.021.238

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?

<P_I,389>

{ED:84._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:Oct._29,_1534.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_022:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
In my right harty maner I commend me vnto your good lordship .
CROMWEL,I,389.022.240

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_022:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And wher as of late the kinges highnes hathe directed his Commyssion
vnto your lordship and other for pullyng downe and reformacion of
certayne anoysaunces made and done by Sir Robart Wyngfeld within the
Marches of Calays , the kinges pleasure is that ye and thother
Commyssioners shall circumspectly viewe and ouersee the same . And that
that of necessite ought to be refourmyd for the welthe <P_I,390>
strengthe and commodite of the sayd Towne and marches accordyng as it
was thought at my last beyng ther to be amendyng , and the resydue that
$neither damagithe ne hurtithe the same Towne to stand still as ye see
reasonable cause after your discresion . and as ye shall seme good .
CROMWEL,I,390.022.241

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_022:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And thus the blessed Trenyte preserue your lordship
CROMWEL,I,390.022.242

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_022:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
At london the xxix day of October . CROMWEL,I,390.022.243

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_022:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your lordshyppis assuryd Freend Thomas Crumwell . CROMWEL,I,390.022.244

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_022:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
{ED:ADD.} To the honourable and my veray good Lorde my lord Vicount
Lisle the kynges Depute of Calais be this youen . CROMWEL,I,390.022.245

<Q_CRO_A_1534_T_TCROMWELL> <L_CROMWEL_023> <A_THOMAS_CROMWELL>
<A-GENDER_MALE> <A-REL_---> <A-DOB_1485?> <R_ARTHUR_LISLE>
<R-GENDER_MALE> <R-REL_---> <R-DOB_--->

<P_I,391>

{ED:86._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:Nov._17_[1534].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My very good lorde aftre my right harty commendacions I am now enforced
to write my mynde plainly vnto youe as to him the preseruation of whose
honour I desire Bothe for the discharge of my dueuty to the kinges
highnes , and for the declaration of myn hartye good will whiche I bere
vnto you , CROMWEL,I,391.023.246

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and therfor I require you my lorde to take it in good parte .
CROMWEL,I,391.023.247

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
First I trust you consider what a charge you haue there vnder the
kinges Maiestie CROMWEL,I,391.023.248

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and I woold youe should remember Both what besemeth a man to doo being
in that place , and that the same conteineth in it no state of
inheritaunce , ne terme for lief But vppon the good Behauiour of the
personne having it . CROMWEL,I,391.023.249

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Nowe if you shuld waye the thing and the nature of it indifferently ,
Wold you thinke it mete that a man shuld haue that charge , which wold
Bring himself to suche necessitie that he shuld be constrayned to put
all thinges to sale , that be commytted vppon speciall trust to his
discreation , neglecting of thone parte the kinges highnes honour to be
preserued in the satisfaction of his graunttes , of thother parte as it
were contempnyng all frieendeship in giving place to a litle Lucre .
CROMWEL,I,391.023.250

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Surely my lorde suche a gouernour as you Be shuld not Bynde himself at
any manes request to performe that shall not percase lye in him , ne by
any his excesse in living make himself soo nedye , that whenne the
present thing shuld happen , he shuld be forced to haue more estimacion
of money thenne regarde to the tayle it Bringeth with it .
CROMWEL,I,391.023.251

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:49?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_023:E1:1534:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
If I were not determyned to contynue your lordships assured Freende I
wold not worke this plainly with you , CROMWEL,I,391.023.252

admynyster and do vnto me and other of his fryndes whiche dothe write

the conveyaunce of Coyne owt of the realme . CROMWEL,I,409.028.285

lorde Chauncelor who Immedyatlye Sent For My lorde cheffe Justyce of
the kynges benche the cheffe Justyce of the Common place the cheffe
Barron and Mr. Fytzeherberd Mr. Attorney Mr. Solysytor and I being
present CROMWEL,I,409.028.286

thinges For the putting the Kynges Subiectes and other in more terroure
ande Feare vppon which deuyse serche was made and a goode estatute

statute made alredye for any suche purpose what myght the Kynges hignes
by the aduyse of his Counsaylle doo to withstande so greate a daunger
lyke as your grace alledgyd at my beyng with you to the which yt was
answeryd by my lorde cheffe Justyce that the Kynges hyghnes by the
aduyse of his Cownsayll myght make proclamacyons and vse all other
polecyes at his pleasure as well in this Case as in Anye other lyke For
the avoyding of any suche daungers and that the sayd proclamacyons and
polyces so deuysyd by the King & his cownsayll for any such purpose
sholde be of as good effect as Any law made by parlyament or otherwyse
which oppynyon I assure your grace I was veray gladde to here wheruppon
the sayd statute was drawen in to a $copy in forme as $a proclamacyon

My veray good lord aftre my moost harty commendacions Thise $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} taduertise youe that vndoubtedly the kinges highnes doth
in soo thankfull sorte accepte your seruice there doon vnto his
maiestie , and in euery condicion soo allowe approve and commende you
wise substanciall and discreate proceding , as like as ye haue moche
cause to reioyse therin , soo shall the same be certain meane and
occasion , that ye shall assuredlye what ende soeuer your busines there
shall take , returne to his highnes as hartely welcom and in as greate
reputacion as youe could yourself desire , wherof for my parte I am
euen for many respectes as gladde as ye canne be yourself .

accustumed maner . Wherby I assure you , ye shall do a meritorious and
very good dede , as god knowith who preserue your lordship .

{ED:143._CROMWELL_TO_[SIR_PIERS_DUTTON,_SHERIFF_OF_CHESHIRE].}

{ED:Apr._3,_1536.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:PIERS_DUTTON:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_039:E1:1536:COPY:OTHER
In my right harty maner I commend me vnto you , CROMWEL,II,8.039.393

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:PIERS_DUTTON:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_039:E1:1536:COPY:OTHER
and where I am Crediblye enformed the oone John Offeley Aboute the
space of ayere paste receyued at Calais of oone Humfrey Lightfote
thenne factor vnto A frende of myne named Edmond Rous ciiii li to be
delyuered over vnto the said Edmonde here in London whiche Som of ciiii
li the said Offeleye contrary to the truste and confidence that he was
put in as yete hath not made Deliuery of but imploiethe & conuerteth
the same vnto his owne vse to the greate hurte & hinderaunce of my said
frende . Beynge nowe aduertysed that the said Ofley hathe merchaundyes
wares & goodes at this present tyme within the Town of Westechester and
other places adyoynynge within the lymite of your office and that the
same Ofeley hathe also personall recorse thether I requyre you and in
the kynges name will and commaunde you that for redresse to be had of
the said detestable wronge & due restytution to be made unto the said
Edmond Rous of his said mony dishonestly and vntrewly kepte from hym by
the said Offeley accordynge to iustice and equite you do immediatelye
after the sight of these my letteres attache & arreste the persone of
the sayd Offeley and oonles the same Offeley shall incontinente
thervpon without delay restore <P_II,9> vnto the said Edmond his said
mony with his resonable damages & expences sustayned by his vntrewe
delynge or otherwyse compownde wythe the said Edmond to kepe the same
Offeley in your salve custodye and to convay hym hyther to london so
shortly as you shall convenyentlye may personally to answere before me
& others of the kinges honorable Covnsayll wherfore he ought not so to
do . And if you shall not can apprehend the persone of the said Offeley
than to arreste his said Goodes and to put the same vndre your salve
custody vntyll the said Offeley shall outher fully restore vnto my said
frend his said Mony or otherwise gyue sufficyente cavtion to answere
hym in the same accordynge to the due ordre of the lawe Shewynge sutche
erneste harty diligence herein as my said frende may by your polycye &
frendeshipp for my sake to be extended vnto hym be conveyed to his said
debt without ferther Svtes or delayes if by any honeste meane you shall
so can compase the same . CROMWEL,II,9.039.394

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:PIERS_DUTTON:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_039:E1:1536:COPY:OTHER
And I shall thaunkefully remembre your doynge herein at my desyre in
case you shall make requeste vnto me at any tyme hereafter .
CROMWEL,II,9.039.395

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:PIERS_DUTTON:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_039:E1:1536:COPY:OTHER

{ED:145._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:Apr._24_[1536].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_040:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Aftre my right harty commendacions your lordship shall herwith receyve
the kinges highnes letteres answering only to the post scripta of yours
by Thadeus lately addressed vnto him . the matier wherof for the
sodaynes of it and the incertaintie of the conditions hath perplexed
his Maiestie that before he wil make any other answer to theffecte of
your said letteres his grace wil knowe the veraye certaintie whither
any suche thing be determyned or noo . CROMWEL,II,10.040.398

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_040:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And therfor it $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} wel doon that ye accelerate
your answer therin asmoche as ye maye with suche other occurrantes as
shal chaunce in the meane tyme . CROMWEL,II,10.040.399

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?

I haue delyuered vnto your seruaunt peter Larke cc=li=

touching the same I doubt not but your wisedom wil considre

<P_II,19>

{ED:153._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:July_5_[1536].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Aftre my right harty commendacions to your Lordshippe I haue receyved
your sundry letteres , for the whiche I doo right hartely thank youe ,
and amonges others those of the xxi=th= of the last moneth , writen for
your answer to a fewe wordes inserted in thende of my letteres a litle
befor addressed vnto youe , touching your contencion for the annuitie
by the <P_II,20> kinges highnes graunted to Maister brian vppon
thattainder of Norres , the cause of whiche your staye or I maye still
call it contencion therin , apperethe in your said letteres not soo
freendely conceyved , as I thinke my merities towardes youe haue
deserued being only your fantazie that I shuld rather of my self thenne
otherwise promote that matier vnto youe . CROMWEL,II,20.041.413

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
For soo ye write , whenne his Maiestie shall give me an expresse
commaundement , and saye my pleasure is thowe shalt paye oon hundreth
poundes to suche an vse etc . CROMWEL,II,20.041.414

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Truly my lord though my talent be not soo precious as yours , yet I
trust with his helpe that gave me it , to vse it soo as it shall doo
his office without gathering suche suspitions vppon freendeship .
CROMWEL,II,20.041.415

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I repete that worde again bicause I ment freendely in the writing of it
, or the adhering soo fast to the ymaginacion therof , that I shuld doo
nothing without expresse commaundementes at his request whose only
inclynacion shuld of congruence bowe thaffections of suche men as we be
. who hathe receyved all that we haue at his hande , and cause vs
rather kindely to give place , thenne soo ernestly to contende as might
percace neyther prevayl ne suffre the thing to haue that grace it might
haue had at the begynning CROMWEL,II,20.041.416

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And yet wold I as oon that toke myself in your oune estimacion for your
freende , desire youe to thinke that I will not wade in any priuate
matier in the king my Souueraign lordes name vnles I haue his
commaundement soo to doo , as in my first letteres writen for the said
Annuite I declared vnto youe I had , whiche of his greate goodnes it
pleasithe his highnes to avouche at this tyme vnto youe .
CROMWEL,II,20.041.417

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But nowe to your letteres . CROMWEL,II,20.041.418

nede and seruice , he wold bestowe it vppon youe ,
CROMWEL,II,21.041.430

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And if the lawe wold allott it vnto you ye said ye trusted his grace
wold permytt vnto youe the vse of your oune , whiche whenne I perceyved
that his Maiestie toke not in very good parte , ne determyned vppon
that gentle dilemma to leave his determynacion imperfite , I wrote vnto
youe freendely aduising youe rather frankly and with an apparance of a
good will to satisfie his grace thenne soo to contende in it , as he
might take it vnkindely . CROMWEL,II,21.041.431

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_041:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

payne to make me beleve that I haue neyther freendeship in me nor
honestie , wherin howe freendely ye procede with me But that ye be
moche given to your oune iudgement , I durst make yourself the Judge .
CROMWEL,II,21.041.432

<P_II,23>

{ED:156._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:July_23_[1536].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_042:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Aftre my right harty commendacions to your Lordshippe , By this currour
ye shall receyve the kinges highnes answer to suche letteres as ye haue
lately dispeched vnto him , theffecte wherof I doubt not but ye will
considre and accomplishe if ye maye as shall appertayn .
CROMWEL,II,23.042.447

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_042:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And forasmoche as by your last letteres of the xij=th= of this moneth
writen to me , I perceyve that vppon myn writen befor touching the
cause of Maister Brian ye were sumwhat moved , gathering what ye could
, and applieng the same if not colerikly I must nedes thinke
melancoulily , to your purpose with chaunge of some of my wordes and
sentences to make your matier the more apparant being yet freendely
disputed , to thintent the matier therof might haue no further mention
, being nowe come to a good ende bothe-2 for the kinges highnes
satisfaction , and the remocion of that hote matier from bothe our
stomakes who be nowe , as for myn oune parte I dare avouche , soo I
think for yours clerely purged , like as I commenced the same freendely
with youe , that is to saye that parte wherin at the lest appered a
contencion Soo , now I require youe , for your parte to finishe
freendely that ye haue promysed as I doubte not but ye will , and to
wrappe vppe the rest in the patent to be made of the same .
CROMWEL,II,23.042.448

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_042:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
For I am for my parte even the same man I was befor , that is your
assured Freende , thoughe in this mater thinking myself a litle touched
I wrote sumwhat quykly , CROMWEL,II,23.042.449

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_042:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and <P_II,24> doubte not in you to fynde the semblable inclynacion
towardes me CROMWEL,II,24.042.450

{ED:188._[CROMWELL]_TO_THE_DUKE_OF_NORFOLK.}

{ED:May_22,_1537.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_HOWARD_II:MALE:_:1473:64
LETTER:CROMWEL_045:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Pleasith it your grace to be aduertised , that the kinges highnes
having received your letteres dated at Birlington the xviii=th= Day of
this moneth , wherby his grace percaiveth your order takyn , for the
same Birlington , and the howse of Gervies , his highnes giving vnto
you alwaies his most herty thankes , hath commaunded me to aduertise
you of his graciouse pleasour , both touching the effecte of the same
your letteres , and also to the maters comprised in your letteres to me
, with certain remembrances deliuered vnto me by leonard Bekwith .
CROMWEL,II,56.045.468

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_HOWARD_II:MALE:_:1473:64
LETTER:CROMWEL_045:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as touching your said order surely the kinges highnes liketh it
veray well . CROMWEL,II,56.045.469

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_HOWARD_II:MALE:_:1473:64
LETTER:CROMWEL_045:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And albeit that he doubteth not , but the persons whom ye haue
appointed woll do euery thing to the best , yet neuertheles forasmoch ,
as by Acte of parliament all landes atteynted must passe by thandes of
the kinges generall Surveyours and certain thinges by the order of the
lawe bothe-2 in fynding off offices & other thinges is to be obserued ,
ye shall understonde that the Kinges highnes at this tyme dothe send
doun certain of his Counsail to take order in that mater , aswell
touching the Fynding off offisses as also to make certayn & perffect
bokes of all thinges belongyng to the same ; not for that they shall
attempt to adnull or infringe eny thing that $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe}
done by you ne by the persons appointed by your lordship , but that
they all to geder may so conferre that euery thing may be perfitely and
duely done to the kinges honour & resonable proffict , his grace
thinking that afore the same $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} directely &
perfictely accomplished , considering the tyme of the yere nowe , and
that fermers commenly entre not but aboutes michaelmas . It shuld not
be for his graces proffict , to make any graunt of any part of the said
landes , vnto the said tyme and also that the same may be well surveyed
at which tyme his highnes woll not onlye haue suche a respect bothe
vnto the pore men Inhabeting abowt Bridlyngton & Jervaux but also forse
for some substaunciall person , mete and necessary to staye the cuntrey
& kepe hospitalite to <P_II,57> dwell in the pryncypall parte of the
monasterye $for whom his highnes is mynded to folowe moch your
lordships advice and counsail , and dothe require you to aduertise hym
Fullye of your oppynyons touching the same . CROMWEL,II,57.045.470

LETTER:CROMWEL_045:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as touching the deposicons takyn of certain women anempst the
cutting doun & buryall of the traytours in Westmoreland & Cumberlande
surely having regard & respect to the evill example & perverse myndes
of the offendours , whiche is thought cam not only of womens heddes but
some men were the principal procurers , the kinges highnes thinketh
veryly , that if the said deposicons had been ernestly takyn , the
plaines of that mater might haue been easely known .
CROMWEL,II,57.045.471

<P_II,58>

{ED:189._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:June_6,_1537.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right herty commendacion Albeit ye have ben hitherto somwhat
slak and negligent to write vnto me and aduertise me from tyme to tyme
of your occurrences and successes yet nevertheles having oportunite to
write vnto you by the bringer herof Monsieur du Vauldray who hath been
here with the Kinges Maieste from the Quene of Hungrye Regen in the
lowe countrees to visite and salute his hieghnes and declare her
excuses of . the conveyance made and geven to the traytour Pole to
conducte hym from Cambray <paren> where <P_II,59> being commaunded by
the frenshe king to avoyde all his dominions he was retyred </paren> to
the dominion of the bishop of liege whiche was thought to have ben more
solemne , then the traytes Requyred . It notwithstanding . his grace
hath taken their excuses in good part . CROMWEL,II,59.046.483

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Nowe at his departure from hens to Themperours Court I have thought to
aduertise you , that Don Diego de mendoza is arrived here . at the
Wodensday next after pentecost resorting to the kinges maieste then
being at Hamptoncourt . was veray honorably met receyved and
entreteyned after the best sorte with the which . and also the other
ambassadeur here resident I and other of the kinges conseill . by his
Maiestes appoinctement have had at sundry tymes conference togeder vpon
the causes of his commyng touching the mariage Wherunto although his
grace bee of good inclination nevertheles as yet there is nothing
concluded Aswell bicause the said Don Diego brought no newe commission
with hym but onely suche as thambassadeur bifore tyme here resident had
receyved long-MSR bifore his commyng As also bicause they seme to make
som difficulte in suche thinges as on our behalf be proposed and
demaunded touching the bishop of Rome . that the said Emperour for his
behalf shal not sticke with his doinges but rather departe from them
and adhere to the kinges maieste , in suche wise that he shuld assent
nor agree to no maner thing that the said bishop or his adherentes wold
attempt agenst his maieste Realme or subiectes or to any displeasure of
thesame but rather lett it and withstand all suche purposes and
enterprises to the vttermost of his power . And as yet have not agreed
therunto . Wherupon the said ambassadours and also vpon other
conferences had with them have writen at this tyme by the said Monsieur
de Vauldray And vpon suche answer . as they shal have from thens agayn
. CROMWEL,II,59.046.484

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
the hole mater $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} or concluded or broken of . as
the cace shal Requyre Wherof . I thinke best and advise you to pretende
ignorance . CROMWEL,II,59.046.485

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Yet nevertheles if ye see good oportunite and occasion offred . ye may
shewe what disposition ye knewe the kinges highnes <paren> vpon good
causes </paren> was at your departure Immutably agenst the said bishop
and that ye doubte not but he shuld not repute hole entiere and perfite
allyance with any person . that wold agree assent or assist hym to any
thing that myght sounde to his graces person Royaulme or subiectes
displeasure sayeng and declaring the same as of your self with the best
circumstances and as discretely as ye can . CROMWEL,II,59.046.486

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Taking hede evermore to the entretenement and norrishing of the good
amytie bitwene them asmoche as ye shall convenyently may and in all
thinges requisite keping yourself as closse as $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe}
expedient vsing in this your charge such good dexterite <P_II,60> and
circumspection as ye knewe our good opinion and expectacion was and
endureth yet ye shuld . CROMWEL,II,60.046.487

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
As concerning of our newes and successes here sithens your departure I
assure you thanckes be to our blessed Creatour the kinges Maieste is in
as good helth , and disposition as I saw hys grace of a long season And
the more bicause the Quenes grace is qwick with childe
CROMWEL,II,60.046.488

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
god by his grace sende her good deliuerance of suche aprince long to
lyve according to his Maiestes graciouse desir and the common Joye and
welth of all his Realme and good feithfull subiectes who for the same
being the newes therof brought from Hamptoncourt hether to london on
Trinitie sondaye at after none there was grete celebrite at Poules and
thanckes geven to god , and in the evenyng solemne fyres made in sundry
places as well of the Citie as of other townes . CROMWEL,II,60.046.489

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_046:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The hole estat of the Realme from the highest to the lowest are in
veray good rest and quiete with their herty obedience and good will $to
the kinges maieste all of oon vnion and concorde suche as have ben
offendours veray sorye for their offences and full desyrouse to have
occasion to ministre the kinges maieste som acceptable seruice for to
shewe their true hert to hym the more conformed for his benign and
graciouse pardon mercyfully extended vpon them which his maieste hath
observed hitherto and woll for ever observe Inviolably .
CROMWEL,II,60.046.490

For although . the Lordes Darcy and Husey . Sirs Robert Constable .

Lomleys son , Robert aske , Nicholas tempest Thabbott of Jervaulx the
priour of byrlington and som other , also Sir Thomas Percy . had their
pardon . yet bicause they have ben openly convinced and attaynted . of
certaine conspiracyes and highe treasons most Ingrately spitefully and
haynously committed agenst his benigne and so graciouse mercyfull
maieste vnto them <paren> as Right was and their Incurable Ingratitudes
deserved </paren> have ben condamned of highe treason , and som of them
alredy executed Wherof if there is any communicacion moved vnto you ye
maye . assuredly afferme that If they had not highely offended sithens
the kinges pardon . his maieste had never remembred their precedent
offenses nor imputed thesame to their charge , Being a prince most
honorable obseruatour of his worde . CROMWEL,II,60.046.491

{ED:192._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:July_6_[1537].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_047:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right herty Commendations to your Lordeshippe Forasmoche as in
the Controuersye depending bitwene the lady Whethel and her sone the
kinges maieste hath directed his commission thether . In consyderacion
that she is a wydowe sole and destitute of Confort I have thought for
the preseruacion of her good right hertely to desyre and praye you that
the rather at myn instance and Requisition ye will beare her your
lawfull favour and support in her good right and title according to the
lawe equite and Justice . So that no part therof be oppressed but the
veray truth appere and have place accordingly . Wherin ye shal doo $a
$veray {TEXT:averay} charitable dede meritoriouse towardes god and to
me acceptable pleasur . CROMWEL,II,62.047.498

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_048:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right herty commendacion Bicause I wold not lett this berer ,
George Pery , oon of the gentilmen of Monsieur Chappuys themperours
ambassadour here resident to departe withoute my letteres vnto you
although I can not amplely aduertise you of all thinges yet for this
present I aduertise that being here at Stepeney this mornyng arryved
hither Rouge Croix the herald which ye sent with your letteres dated
the xxiij=th= daye of June last CROMWEL,II,63.048.503

berer infourme you of it . CROMWEL,II,63.048.504

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34

thankes taking your excuses for your so late writing in good parte .

{ED:213._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:Sept._24_[1537].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_049:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my moste hartie commendacions . Where as oon John brymedgham oon
of the Kinges subiectes of Irlande was <P_II,_80> robbed of Late vpon
the see of his shipp and also goodes by certain espaynyardes , For the
restytucion wherof vpon complaynt made to the kingis highnes .
Themperours Ambassadours here hath ernestly written to the Justices of
that cuntrey . Leaste the same doo not take effecte there according to
the due order of Justice and the said partie may fortune to be driven
to seke further for remedie in that parties , this $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} hartly to deasire you in that case Soo to purpose his
cause and matier there with the emperours Counsaile , as the said
brymedgham may haue Justice administred vnto him in the premisses
accordingly . And further to doo therin , as my lorde Butler hath more
at Large declared in his letteres to you at this tyme , who as fully
instructed in that matier hath at leynght written vnto you for the same
. vnto whome I pray you to give ferme and vndoubtid credence .
CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_049:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And thus hartly fare ye well . CROMWEL,II,_ID

<P_II,90>

{ED:219._[CROMWELL]_TO_[THE_DUKE_OF_NORFOLK].}

{ED:[Jan.-Sept._1537.]}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_HOWARD_II:MALE:_:1473:64
LETTER:CROMWEL_050:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right harty commendacions to your lordship wheras the kinges
highnes hathe given the keping of his castle of Bamburghe vnto this
berer Maistr Horseley forasmoche as his grace is enformed that the said
Castle is soo farre in decaye that without some reparacion to be
presently doon vppon it , it canne not be enhabited , his graces
pleasure is that your lordship shall cause some oone or two of the
consail there to ride to the said Castle and to vueu the state therof
and what reparacions must be necessarily doon out of hande vppon the
same to make it habitable , and making theruppon an estimate of the
charges to aduertise his majeste of their doinges therin accordingly
forseing that they procede in this matier with suche dexteritie as in
the reparacions to be doon for the dwelling of the keper , they haue
only respecte to the necessitie therof and not to any thing to be doon
for pleasure or suche commoditie as may be spared .
CROMWEL,II,90.050.535

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_HOWARD_II:MALE:_:1473:64
LETTER:CROMWEL_050:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And thus Fare you $well . CROMWEL,II,90.050.536

{ED:223._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

After my right herty commendacion This $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} to
aduertise you that sithens the Departure of Rouge croix whiche was
despeched to you in post on wesnesday last here be no newes occurrantes
but veray good newes which for suretie I have receyved this mornyng ,
that it hath pleased allmyghty god of his goodnes to sende vnto the
Quenes grace delyvraunce of a goodly prince to the grete confort
Reioysse and consolacion of the Kinges Maieste and of all vs his most
humble loving and obedient subiectes Wherof we have veray grete cause
to thancke our most benigne and graciouse creatour , who after so long
expectacion hath exalced our prayours and desyres CROMWEL,II,94.051.537

{ED:224._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:Oct._20_[1537].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_052:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Maister Wiat aftre my right harty commendacions bicause it hathe
pleased the kinges Maieste to addresse this berer to Themperour to
signifie vnto him the certain newes of the birthe of the prince ,
knowing that his instruction to you $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} sufficient
without further repeticion of the same , I shall forbere to molest you
with long letteres and only require you to handle your last commission
in suche discrete and temperate sorte , as at the returne of this said
Berer Mr. Dudley your good Freende , his highnes may perceyve that
thing whiche his grace desirethe to knowe that is themperours good
inclynacion towardes his Maieste or the contrary if it shall otherwise
appere vnto you . CROMWEL,II,95.052.544

Maister Wiat aftre my right harty commendacions Albeit I haue at this
tyme no matier of importance to be writen vnto you , yet having
thoportunytie of this messanger being as I vndrestonde dispeched vnto
you for your oune priuate affaires , I thought mete to signifie , that
your last letteres conteyning your conferences with themperour and with
Monsieur de Grandevile , were taken and accepted in as thankfull parte
, as I haue lightly seen {in}_P the letteres of any the kinges Maiestes
Oratours , residyng in outwarde partes . CROMWEL,II,102.053.552

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_053:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

instant request and sute for money for your Diettes , As vppon
tharryval of your said letteres I toke ordre for the payment of your
diettes for vi monethes beforhande , for the present payment of all
suche money as you had layd out for postes , and for your further diett
for two monethes to be receyved in the lieu of a prest for the dispeche
of suche postes as you shuld addresse hither . CROMWEL,II,102.053.553

LETTER:CROMWEL_053:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Postscripta wheras in your said last letteres addressed to the kinges
Maieste , you doo signifie in the repeticion of your conference with
Themperour that the same shuld saye vnto you vppon your ouerture for
the mediacion of a peax betwen him and the Frenche king , I $can $not
{TEXT:cannot} tel howe my Freendes doo sollicite me alwaye to peax .
For diuerse haue medled in the same , and whenne soeuer my matiers goo
any thing darkely forwarde , I here no worde of mediacion of peax . And
nowe whenne it semeth my successes com summe thing hansomly to passe I
am sollicited to the peax bothe by the king your Maister and by others
. The kinges highnes pleasure is , that vppon the receipt herof taking
your occasion to entre a newe conference and communication with
themperour you shal declare vnto him , that for as moche as in your
late discours with his Maieste , whiche you wrote vnto the kinges
highnes , It appered by the wordes expressed , that he thought , he was
sollicited to the peax whenne his affaires went prosperously <P_II,104>
forwarde , and otherwise harde no mencion of it . As the kinges Maieste
having no respecte to the state of his affaires at that motion of it ,
but to the good of the thing , vppon the zeale he had to bothe princes
, and to the general quiet and repose of all christiendom , made that
ouerture like a good prince and an assured Freende to themperour Soo
being sithens tharrival of your said letteres aduertised of
thabassement of his affaires in Italy , and of the victories of the
frenche king , bothe in the getting of the passage at Zuse , and in the
reenforcing and revitailing of his holdes and Fortresses in those
parties , to declare howe moche his grace tendred the benefite of peax
, and howe litle he regarded any affection or cause that might move him
to fauour either thone or thother parte more thenne becam a prince
indifferent , and soo indifferent that knowing them both to be princes
of honour and his Dere Freendes and Allyes , he could haue been content
with his travail charge and greate expenses to haue been the meane to
conveye them to a quiet , wherby the effusion of christien bloodde
shuld haue been exchued CROMWEL,II,104.053.581

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_053:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Albeit his most noble vertuous and princely overture therin was not soo
lovingly embraced as the dexteritie of the same required . Yet
neuertheles to expresse , that the same proceded vppon the mynde and
zeale declared . CROMWEL,II,104.053.582

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_053:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
His Maieste hath commaunded you eftsones to renovel the said Ouerture
of mediacion vnto him , and to desire him even nowe thoughe his thinges
be not so prosperous altogither as they were to signifie his resolucion
vnto you , whither he canne be content to commytt the decision of his
matiers to his grace Arbitre , if the Frenche king woll for his parte
condescende to doo the semblable . CROMWEL,II,104.053.583

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_053:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And if he woll therunto conforme himself you may thenne require him for
the declaracion of his titles to addresse vnto the kinges highnes suche
a personage as shal be hable sufficiently to instructe his Maieste in
the same the same to bring with him suche commission as he may make
suche ouertures for that purpose as may be reasonable , and semely for
that prince to grounde himself vppon , whiche indifferently desirethe
an honest ende betwene them . Wherupon the frenche king doing the
semblable if he woll agre to the like of this ouerture neither of them
shal nede to doubt , but his Maieste woll so procede betwene them as
neither partie shal haue cause iustly to be greved .
CROMWEL,II,104.053.584

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_053:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And with this matier you may also declare vnto him , howe thinformacion
made that his Oratours here could not haue audience in vi monethes was
vntruly surmytted vnto him , as they haue themselfes confessed , whiche
I thinke thay haue also signified thither for the <P_II,105>
manifestacion of the truth in that behaulf Tempering your wordes soo as
he may take thise aduertisementes and overtures as freendely as they be
made vnto him . And yet soo obseruyng him , in the vttering of his
answers therunto , as you may sumwhat desciphre the botom of his harte
and affection towardes the kinges Maieste , if by any wisedom it may be
drawen out of the same . CROMWEL,II,105.053.585

{ED:234._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:Dec._26_[1537].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_054:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Maister Wiat aftre my right harty commendacions By this berer you shall
receyve the kinges highnes letteres with a commission wherby you be
auctorised to treate commen and conclude with those princes for his
graces parte , as by the said letteres is limited .
CROMWEL,II,110.054.591

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?

the said letteres with suche a dexteritie as theffecte desired may
ensue of the same . CROMWEL,II,110.054.592

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:52?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:34
LETTER:CROMWEL_054:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
there was neuer a better inclynacion in the kinges Maieste both to
forget all thinges passed , to entre a perfite reconsiliacion , and to
doo in all thinges that may turne to Themperours honour or commoditie ,
asmoche as canne be reasonably desired of him , thenne there is at this
present , if Themperour woll nowe shewe himself to esteme his highnes
as he pretendeth , and specially in folowing of his graces aduise in
the matier of the counsail CROMWEL,II,110.054.593

all things I doubt not shall soo succede betwene them , as shal be to
goddes glory , to both their honours and to the greate good and quiet
of Christendom CROMWEL,II,110.054.594

{ED:240._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:Feb._15,_1538.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_056:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right hartye commendacions to your lordshipp Forasmoche as I
knowe right well that ye wyll ernestly employe your good dexteryte to
set furthe the contentes of the kinges hieghnes Letteres which ye shall
Receyve at this tyme as yn the lyke ye haue ever accustumed , I haue
thought by these presentes onely to aduertys youe that Albeyt his
hieghnes maketh in the same a Longer Rehersall and discourse of his
matyers thenne percace $you shall thinke to haue been necessary and
rather wrytteth to note and ympute vnto youe some obliuion or
forgetfulnes then for anny greate consequence that may folowe of the
same , yet neuertheles ye may be assuered that his Maiestye berethe no
suche displeasure vnto youe nor entendeth to impute vnto you thereby
suche slaknes as the discourse seamethe to emplye knowing and waying
your truthe , fydelyte and effectuell good wyll and deuocion to his
Maiestye and his affaires , CROMWEL,II,115.056.606

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_056:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But rather his hieghnes thinkethe ye shall thereby vnderstande that he
kepethe in memorye and Rememberaunce an accompte of his affayres and
the hole trayne thereof , by reason of the which his grace signifieth
vnto youe that ye shal doo the lyke to thentent ye may be alwayes the
more redy and the better prepared to make suche aunswere to every poynt
thereof as may be to the Furtheraunce of his matyers of Importaunce
Whenne the cace shall soo Require . CROMWEL,II,115.056.607

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_056:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Therefore I Pray you to take his graces meanyng non otherwyse thenne
soo Nothing <P_II,116> doubting of the contynuaunce of his favour
towardes you , with no lesse Respect and consyderatyon to be had
thereof to your comfort and consolacion yn tyme cummyng thenne your
good merytes doo deserue CROMWEL,II,116.056.608
