{ED:244._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:March_1_[1538].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
Mr. Wiat after my hartie commendations this $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe}
tadvertise you that this present day being the last of February
<P_II,_123> arrived here at the court the bisshop of tarbez being
addressed to the kinges Maiestie from the Frenche King who bringing
with him a commission to entreate and conclude vppon a confirmacion of
al Amities betwene them with an addicion of all suche thinges as on
eyther parte might be divised further to {ED:BLANK} or eyther of their
commodities made playne and certeyn overture that whither the kinges
Majesty wold enter any suche capitulacion or no in cace it shuld be his
pleasure to take it vpon him he shuld for the French kinges parte haue
the hole and entier manyeng of the Peax betwen him and Themperor
CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
and further he offerd on the French kinges behaulf that he shuld never
take peax with themperour but the kinges Majesty shuld therin be a
principall contrahent and also in the matier of counseil and $all other
thinges that the king shuld finde the french king so assured and
confourmable towardes him as he $should $have {TEXT:shuldhaue} cause to
accept him for his good brother and most entier frende , CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
to this the king $answered that there wordes were many tymes so
qualified that it appered hard to him to give any grete credite without
further prouf vnto them CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
nevertheles for that {TEXT:that} {ED:SIC} parte whiche shewed an
effeccion in the said french king the king gave vnto him his condigne
thankes declaring how muche his hieghnes desired the succeding of suche
vniversel peax as might redound to the quiet of all christendome and
how ernestly his grace hath travailed vpon that zele only to obteyne
the mediacion of it not doughting but in cace he wold stike to that
overture his good brother themperour who hath shewed therin alredy good
inclinacion wold right gladly do the semblable CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
and as touching the ioyning of his grace as a principal contrahent to
his Majesty told him that he was assured so to be by the saide
Emperours meanes though the french king wold say nay vnto it , albeit
his overture therin and in the rest carieng with it a frendly visage
was suche as he wold not but take in good parte and give vnto him
thankes also for it , as thankes be given for frendly wordes which kepe
their place as long as they $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} not denied by
contrary effectes . CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
To this they replied that for the french kinges part they could affirme
that as his overtures proceded from a most frendly harte so his dedes
shuld moost certenly approve and confirme the same , CROMWEL,II,_ID

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
but as for Themperour they sayde they could affirme also vpon their
<P_II,124> certeyn knowleage that what wordes soever he had vtterd or
eny for him he never minded to ioyne the king as a primier contrahent
ne wold in any wise agre that the king shuld haue in his hand the
mainieng of the peax betwene them wherunto I assure you the king made
frendly answer for themperours honour trouth and assurednes to the
obseruacion of his worde and in the debating of his most hartie love
towardes themperour , so that our Ambassadours from the frenche king be
retired to London without doing of any thing or ther receyving of any
other answer , CROMWEL,II,124.057.623

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_057:E1:1538:COPY:OTHER
and forasmuch as I do perceyve that they woll offer wonders to stey the
king from themperour albeit I am in most assured hope that they shall
therin faile in their purpos notwithstanding his grace wold I thinke
labor to make some good ende betwen them and therfor the good of
christendom and the better chastesing of the common enemye of the same
, yet I thought good to advertise you therin that you may at your
oportunitie declare the same to $themperor and to his counseil for the

{ED:245._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_058:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right harty commendacion vnto your good lordship thiese be to
aduertise you that the kinges pleasure ys that my seruaunt George Rows
berer herof shall passe out of this Realme into the parties of beyond
the See for his affayres and busynes ther to be done . Withe one
seruaunt and two horses or geldynges twenty poundes in money and other
his laufull cariage and utensiles . And without any vnlawfull serche
let or ympedyment , Wherfore I require you to cause that he may so
passe without any disturbaunce accordyng to the kynges pleasure in that
behalf . CROMWEL,II,126.058.644

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_058:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Thus the blessed Trenyte preserue your good lordship .
CROMWEL,II,126.058.645

<P_II,136>

{ED:255._CROMWELL_TO_GARDINER.}

{ED:Apr._24,_1538.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_061:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Aftre my right harty commendacions to your lordshippe Bicause the
repeticion of suche contencyous matier as hathe been writen betwene vs
shuld be but displeasant and noysome to bothe parties , I shall laye
the same aparte , and for an entre to our former facions of writing ,
only aduertise youe that howesoeuer you haue taken me , I haue shewed
myself your freende whenne the tyme and occasion hathe serued , and
haue not writen more at any season vnto you in any matier thenne the
kinges highnes hathe befor the sending of it furthe perused ,
CROMWEL,II,136.061.685

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_061:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And therfor I thought meself the more touched , that for my gentlenes I
shuld receyve suche vnkinde answers . CROMWEL,II,136.061.686

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_061:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But as I haue nowe given place to your courage , soo I shall put those
matiers in obliuion that haue thus passed betwene vs
CROMWEL,II,136.061.687

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:STEPHEN_GARDINER:MALE:_:1497?:41?
LETTER:CROMWEL_061:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And soo Fare you hartely well CROMWEL,II,136.061.688

kinges hieghnes letteres signifying an ouerture made vnto his Maiestie
by the Frenche King with an Instruccion howe you shall vse and behaue
yourselfes in the same whiche I doubt not you woll duely waye and
consider And so procede therein whether it be proponed according to the
diuise or obiected vnto you , as his Maiesties honour may be preserued
and his commoditie therewith wrought to his graces satisfactyon .
CROMWEL,II,137.062.692

of affaires <P_II,138> nowe in treatie amonges christien princes ,

{ED:259._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_RICHARD_RICHE.}

RECIPIENT:RICHARD_RICH:MALE:_:1497:41
LETTER:CROMWEL_063:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right harty commendations thes bee to aduertise yow , thatt
for suche reasonable causes as the commissionars haue more att large
informyd me of , I haue appoyntyd the late Abbot of Kenellworth for his
pension one hundred pownd yerly during his lif to bee payed vnto hym
att lyke dayes and after lyke sorte as the same is accustomyd {at}_P to
bee payed to others in his case . praying you ondilayedly to cause his
sayd pension to bee entryd in your bookes and his assurance to be
sealyd vppon the same as spedyly as yow may . CROMWEL,II,139.063.699

<P_II,139>

{ED:260._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:May_6_[1538].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_064:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right hartie Commendacions to your Lordshipp Where I am
aduertised that of late it hathe been Signifyed from thens to my lorde
of Herforde , Maister Threasourer of the kinges Maiesties Houshold
Maister brown and others That the Towne of Calys shuld be in som
misorder by certayn Sacramentaries alleaged to be in the same , I $can
$not {TEXT:cannot} a litle mervail that your Lordshipp having good
knowleage and experience of my good wil and contynuel desire to the
repression of errours and to thestablishment of oon perfyt unytie in
opinion amonges vs al the kinges Maiestes people and Subiectes wold not
vouchsauf to gyve me some knowleage if there be any suche Lewde persons
amonges you . CROMWEL,II,139.064.704

<P_II,140>

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_064:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I doubt not but your Lordshipp knoweth bothe howe moche I doo esteame
that the kinges hieghnes towne as my dueutie requyreth and howe wel I
haue <paren> I thank god </paren> hitherto considered what daunger
might ensue vnto it , by Diuersite of opinion specially in mattiers soo
high and weightye doing ever myn office as I might to quiet al thinges
with an honest charite that haue Lightly insurged amonges you .
CROMWEL,II,140.064.705

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_064:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But leaving this parte I shal addresse my self to my purpose which is
to Signefye vnto you that the kinges Maiestie being desirous to knowe
the truthe of these mattiers hath willed and commaunded me to write
vnto you and to the rest of his Counseil there that you shal assemble
yourselfes togither and make due and circumspect inquisicion of this
and al other suche matiers as doo or may in anywise interupt the quiet
and vnyte that shuld be there amonges you . And of the same to aduertis
agayn with convenient diligens by this Berer whom I haue sent thither
for that purpose Having suche regarde to the serious and iuste
examynation and handeling thereof as his Maiestie may see the perfyt
truth dyuided from mennes corrupt affections of fauour malyce or
displeasur . Which shal bothe moche advaunce the reformation of thinges
if it soo require , and declare you which be put in trust there to be
men of that sorte that shal beseame you towardes the mayntenaunce of
trouth and honestie and the Repression of the contrary as apperteynith
. CROMWEL,II,140.064.706

<P_II,148>

{ED:268._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:July_16_[1538].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_068:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right herty commendacions to your lordeship I have receyved
sundry your letteres and right well pervsed and noted the contentes
thereof Wherby I perceyve that in the same the kinges Towne of Calais
there is some Infection of certain persones denyeng the holy sacrament
of Christes blessed body and blud of suche opinion as commonly they
calle Sacramentaries For remedy whereof the kinges graciouse pleasur is
that ye shal cause the said persones suspected to be thoroughly
groundely and substancially examyned aswell vpon the formal as material
poinctes thereof and well weyeng there sayenges CROMWEL,II,148.068.739

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_068:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
In case it shal appere vnto you that they woll maynteyne any errours
agenst the true doctrine ye shal not only cause them to be punyshed to
thexemple of all others but also provide that no suche errours
perniciouse be spradd abrode there but vtterly suppressed banished and
extincted as it apperteyneth . CROMWEL,II,148.068.740

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_

and there allegacions heard on both parties And therupon $suche

$expedient ... inges therin taduertise me with convenient diligence to
thintent I may signefie the same to the kinges Maiestie and therupon

{ED:271._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:Aug._9_[1538].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_070:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right harty recommendacions vnto your good lordship thiese
$shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} to aduertise thesame that I haue resceyved
your letteres of the vi=th= day of this present monthe wherin ye write
concernyng the hoy that was taken by the Frenchemen laden with the
kynges tymber . CROMWEL,II,150.070.755

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_070:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And before the receipt therof I have opteyned a lettere of the
Ambassadour of Fraunce directed to the vicount of diepe for the
restitucion of thesame whiche I send unto your lordship by the berer
herof to thentent ye may send furthe thesame with all spede and
celerite , and that it may please your lordship to aduertise me what
expedicon ye shall haue in that behalfe . CROMWEL,II,150.070.756

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_070:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

At london the ix=th= day of August . CROMWEL,II,150.070.758

<P_II,157>

{ED:276._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:Oct._16,_1538.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my right herty commendacions After the receipte of your letteres
by Mr. Masson vpon the significacion made to the Kinges Maieste by the
Quene Regente of the receipte of Themperours commission and of his good
& singular affection to procede syncerely and conclude all thinges as
their amytie Requireth . The Kinges highnes after the sending of Mr.
Wrysley and Mr. Vaughan in to Flaundres with commission and power to
treatie and conclude with the said Regente hath advised ernestly to
Joyne with themperour . CROMWEL,II,157.071.761

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and therfor despeched this berer his trusty seruaunt Mr. Hobby oon of
the gromes of his graces pryve chambre with letteres and Instructions .
CROMWEL,II,157.071.762

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
His grace thanking you for your grete diligence and dexterite
heretofore vsed Requireth you at this tyme ernestly to procede to the
declaracion of his good affection and purpose whiche I assure you is as
syncere and fervent ernest and effectuel as could be desired and also
of the hole Instructions whiche do procede of the very botome of his
good hert and pure stomacke CROMWEL,II,157.071.763

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Nowe is the tyme that by thesame ye may moche further the matiers and
gett yourself moche prayse and estimacion the which I wold be gladd for
CROMWEL,II,157.071.764

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
the desire I have of your furtherance no lesse then ever I hadd myght
be accomplished and don bifore March CROMWEL,II,157.071.765

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
for at that tyme I trust according to your desire to gett you leave to
com hither agayn and that the Kinges Maieste shal sende som other to
supplie your Rowme there wherfor assaye so ernestly to sett those
thinges foreward . as ye maye encreace your estimacion therby
CROMWEL,II,157.071.766

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The kinges highnes <P_II,158> had sent masson vnto you in stede of this
said berer were it not the chaunce that he is evill diseased of a fever
like as by his owne letteres ye shal perceyve . CROMWEL,II,158.071.767

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
All occurrences here the said Mr. Hobby maye declare vnto you at large
and amplely CROMWEL,II,158.071.768

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I mistrust not your diligence Wherfor withoute longer exhortacion I
commende you to our blessed creatour who sende you prosperite & long
liff CROMWEL,II,158.071.769

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
From london this xvi=th= of October the xxx=th= yere of his graces most
noble Regne CROMWEL,II,158.071.770

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35
LETTER:CROMWEL_071:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Your assuryd louyng Freend Thomas Crumwell CROMWEL,II,158.071.771

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:35

CROMWEL,II,158.071.772

After my right herty commendacions I have receyved your letteres , by
this bearer Nicolas and sett furth the matier of your Retourn at Marche
next CROMWEL,II,166.072.773

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_072:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

perceyve by the kinges letteres who maieste taketh your diligence and
active alacrite there in good part sending you answer of his graces
pleasure in all thinges as by his said letteres ye shal perceyve
CROMWEL,II,166.072.774

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36

furth thereof as ye have don hitherto . CROMWEL,II,166.072.775

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36

I advise you to take <P_II,167> patiently your abode there tyll Aprill
and to sende me worde what money ye shal nede to have sent vnto you

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_072:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Assuring you that I could not see you that went and hath abyden there
honestly furnished to Retourne home and at the later ende to retourne
nedy and disfurnished I do better tender the kinges honour .
CROMWEL,II,167.072.778

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

<P_II,176>

{ED:288._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:Feb._5_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My most bounden dutie with all Reuerence , right humbly remembred to
your Maiestie . CROMWEL,II,176.073.793

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please thesame to knowe that this present mornyng Mons=r= de Castillon
hath bene with me , and declared that yesterdaye he receyved letteres
from the king his Master conteynyng answere to suche matiers as your
highnes did geve hym charge to write of The whiche he wold be gladd he
myght as sone as could be declare declare {ED:SIC} vnto your graces
self afore he shuld make any man participaunt thereof Requiring me
therfore to be his meane that he myght have your graces favorable
audience assone as could be possible and to knowe your graciouse
pleasure therupon CROMWEL,II,176.073.794

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
In general he affirmeth vnto me that his Master counsydering the
manyfold kyndnes and good turnes often receyved of your highnes geveth
suche frendely amyable and gentil answere as may be desired accordingly
CROMWEL,II,176.073.795

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But as touching the declaration of the special poinctes he shewed
hymself so loth to declare them to me afore he had exposed them to your
maieste that I could not conveniently with honeste presse hym of
thesame CROMWEL,II,176.073.796

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
yet nevertheles I have amonges communications at large sucked of hym ,
that his Master woll he shuld shortely retourne thither to hym and that
bitwene Themperour and hym there is no conclusion as yet taken , nor
$shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} afore his retourne from hens to his saide
Master and after conference had with hym in the whiche the said
Castillon promissethe so to employe hym self that there shall folowe of
his going as he trusteth , many good effectes , and moche to the
commoditie both-6 of your highnes and his Master , Albeit I perceyve by
his communication that he locketh not to retourne to be resident here
but that some other $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} sent in his stede
CROMWEL,II,176.073.797

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Further wading with hym , he hath shewed vnto me that the bishop of
Rome wold have established a Legat in Fraunce as it was wount to be but
that his Master hath refused it and woll in no maner wise consente
therto . CROMWEL,II,176.073.798

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I lyke well that begynnyng vpon occasion of the same we commoned of
your grace howe litel ye regarded any the said bishops vniust censures
, and that I trusted other princes wold regarde them the like ,
CROMWEL,II,176.073.799

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And yet further I casted in his worttes that if they wold regarde them
your highnes was and shuld be hable both to defende and kepe yourself
vpright and offende sore such as wold offende your maiestie and that in
thesame cace they shuld <P_II,177> not fynde your grace unfournished of
all thinges expedient Wherupon I toke occasion to bring hym vp to myn
armary and have shewed vnto hym such store of harneys and wepens as I
have the whiche he semed to esteme moche CROMWEL,II,177.073.800

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and I tolde hym that there were other particular armaryes of the lordes
and gentilmen of this Royaulme more then the nombre of Twenty aswell or
better furnyshed then myn was wherat he woundred and sayd that he
thought your grace the prince best furnished thereof in Christendom
CROMWEL,II,177.073.801

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
We commoned of the cafart Cornibus that slaunderose frere
CROMWEL,II,177.073.802

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
He said that your Maiesties Ambassadour the bishop of Hereford hath
sued and proposed certayn articles against hym , the copie whereof he
hath promessed to sende vnto me : And further that the said bishop hath
bene very playn and Rownde with Messieurs of the counseill there .
CROMWEL,II,177.073.803

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I have promessed vnto hym that I shuld with all diligence sende to
knowe your graciouse pleasure touching his audience and Incontinently
to geve vnto hym knowlege thereof CROMWEL,II,177.073.804

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Therfore I beseche most humbly your Maiestie to take this my rude
letteres and procedinges in good $part and to vouchesauf to aduertise
me of your graciouse pleasure vpon thesame and all other thinges being
assured that in thaccomplishement of the same and all other thinges
committed to my charge I shall employe and endevoir meself most
ernestly with all my power according to your most abundaunt benignite
towardes me your most humble seruaunt and as to my most bounden duetie
it apparteyneth . CROMWEL,II,177.073.805

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The saide Castillon is moche desyrouse of spede CROMWEL,II,177.073.806

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and If it were possible to have your fauorable audience tomorowe he
wold fayne see that your Maiestes most noble Joyell my lorde princes
grace . Wherby my pover advice is vnder your graciouse correction .
that <paren> if your highnes could have convenient leasure </paren> it
shuld be best to appoincte it tomorowe . CROMWEL,II,177.073.807

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_073:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Nevertheles your high wisedome can better Juge what is most expedient ,
CROMWEL,II,177.073.808

My Lord after most herty and affectuouse commendacions I do at this
tyme by the kinges gracious commandment <P_II,184> aduertise you that
besides the knowlege of suche thinges as ye shal have by my letteres
sent lately vnto you by your seruaunt Gowgh we have aduertisement that
not only there be sundry pyrattes in the see commen out of the partes
of Holand and Zeland to thintent to robbe the kings subiectes but also
that on Ashewenesday last all maner ships of what nation soeuer they be
, noon excepted , were by proclamacion made on Themperours behalf in
Antwerp and elleswhere arrested tyll Easter and further tyll they knowe
Themperours pleasure wherupon as yet our ambassidour there can not
knowe for any sute whether our ships be comprehended therin or noo
CROMWEL,II,184.075.836

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_075:E1:1539:COPY:OTHER
But for all surities the kings maieste hath caused for the same and
other consyderacions all shippes and crayers thorough this hole Realme
to be arrested and of all nations whatsoeuer they be so that without
his graces special leave they shal have no licence to departe nor any
passage $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} suffred to go from hens to any part
beyond the see withoute his graces licence tyll we shall knowe further
. CROMWEL,II,184.075.837

{ED:294._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:Mar._10_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_076:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Mr. Wyat after my right affectuouse commendations . I have receyved not
onely your letteres sent hither by Nicolas the Currour and by your
seruaunt Rudston but also all other conteyned in your cataloge at the
later ende of my letteres sent by the said Nicolas .
CROMWEL,II,185.076.857

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_076:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Ye may perceyve by the kinges letteres to you addressed at this tyme ,
howe thankefully his grace accepteth your good diligence and doynges
there And also thoccurrences and bruytes which have ben spredd abrode
merveillouse strange the suspicion and coniecture of those shippes
which be sent owt of flanders to Spayne for what cause no man can well
tell here And tharrest of ships in Flaundres CROMWEL,II,185.076.858

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_076:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Albeit sithens the kinges letteres signed I have receyved aduertisement
from Mr. Wryothesley that as Wenesdaye last the Quene Regen and the
counseill there sent hym iiij warauntes for the delyverey of the same
shippes . but as yet they be not arryved . CROMWEL,II,185.076.859

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_076:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
We can not satisfie our <P_II,186> myndes whereof did procede all those
vnkynd partes and such strangenes as sodenly and vpon no maner ground
hath ben sithens lent vsed to the said Mr. Wryothesley .
CROMWEL,II,186.076.860

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36

he had good chere and entretenement a litel afor that ii currours shuld
arryve thither from Spayn CROMWEL,II,186.076.861

whither Themperour wrote any suche thinges to be doon we $can $not

Frenshemen , and bishop of Rome . And if ye can perceyve any notable

have to theffect of the kinges letteres nowe vnto you .
CROMWEL,II,186.076.864

and with as good diligence as I can , to thintent ye may retourne
hither according to your desyre CROMWEL,II,186.076.865

{ED:297._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:Mar._14_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_077:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My most bounden duetie to your most excellent maieste with all honour
and Reverence right humbly offred Please it thesame to be aduertised
that I have receyved such letteres as were directed to me both-3 from
your graces oratours the bishop of Rome and Mr. Wryothesley the whiche
I have diligently Readen and pervsed And not onely according to your
graciouse pleasure Directed my letteres to the bishop of Hereforde ,
conteyning in effect the thre poinctes signified vnto me by Mr.
Sadleyers letteres on your graces behaulf . CROMWEL,II,192.077.871

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_077:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I thought better to despeche them by my private letteres . then to put
your highnes to the payne to have writen and troubled your self with
thesame . CROMWEL,II,192.077.872

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_077:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
To Mr. Wryothesley I had writen afore that he shuld accelerate his
retourne with all spedy diligence so that he myght be assone retourned
at Calais as Chappuys shuld arryve thither or bifore . Bicause I have
on your maiesties behalf contremaunded your Maiesties deputie there
that in cace the said Chappuys shuld arryve there bifore Mr.
Wryothesleys cummyng the said deputie vnder colour of $honourable and
kynd entretenement shuld honestly and as it were for to shewe hym
gentilnes and make hym good chere to kepe hym and reteyn hym there
vntyll he shuld be sure of Mr. Wryothesley arrivaill at Calais or
within the marches of the same withoute any daunger And in cace that
the said Chappuys could not be that waye persuaded to tarye but
Instantely desire to departe that then the said depute shuld playnely
saye vnto hym that forasmoche as he had a certain general restraincte
bifore this and afore the date of his passeport he desireth him to tary
tyll he shuld knowe your graces pleasure being vpon the very see syde
and where he shuld have euery tyde oportunite to sende and receyve
answere , or vntyll the said Wryothesley shuld be arryved .
CROMWEL,II,192.077.873

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_077:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But as I thinke my letteres to the said depute shal not nede to be put
in vre CROMWEL,II,192.077.874

LETTER:CROMWEL_077:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
This day being my lord Chancelour My lorde of Sussex and the bishop of
Duresme with my I have receyved letteres from the president and
conseillers of your graces counseill in the North . dated ix=o= Marcij
conteyning that a certain frenshe ship laden with Scotishe goodes
wetherdryven at South schelis in the countie of Duresme whereof therle
of Westmerland having aduertisement And by certain persons from
Scotland advice geven afore serched the ship . Found vnder the bagages
in the botom thereof a nest of Traytours that is to saye oon Robert
more preste of Chicester which was lately scappid from Hexams prison .
And Two Irishe men a monke and a frere who had with them sediciouse and
Trayterouse letteres agenst your grace directed to the bishop of Rome
and to the traytour Pole Amonges the which there was oone from that
yong rebell trayter Fitzgerald to the cardinal Pole conteynyng the
kyndnes he had founde in hym and in his and requiring him not to put
him in obliuion . CROMWEL,II,193.077.888

But beleve the said monke . CROMWEL,II,193.077.889

Indultes or expeditions obteyned there shuld take mo effecte in
Scotland withoute the licence of their prince . The which purpose I
like well trusting that the mercy of god woll extende his brightnes
vpon them to perceyve the truth of his word and gospell to the bishops
confusion . CROMWEL,II,194.077.900

then the duke of Saxony shuld be heyer having maryed theldest doughter
And that he is aduertised that by a general assent of the hole
countreys that in this cace the duk of Saxony shuld enioye all And
further that the dukdoms of Cleves Julik Berghes and Gheldres have made
an allyaunce and promesse to stycke all togeder and hold oone with an

{ED:298._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:Mar._17_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_078:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my most bounden duetie of honour and reverence most humbly
remembred Please it your excellente Maiestie <P_II,196> to witte that
according to your graciouse pleasure I and other of your graces
honorable counseill are ernestly employed to fulfylle your highnes
pleasure signified vnto vs and suche charges as we have of your Royall
Maiestie in suche wise that at your return all thinges $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} in as good forewardnes as may be . CROMWEL,II,196.078.931

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_078:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My lorde Admyrall hath aduertised me by his letteres , that he is
aboute and hath bene with most celerite for his part to fulfyll the
same . CROMWEL,II,196.078.932

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_078:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
He had aduertisement that in all Normandye nor in the ryver of Roan
there were no ships of werre nor preparacions of any but that their was
an ydell bruyt nothing like to be true that some ships shuld assemblee
and gather togither at Brest in Bretayne . Albeit there is no suche
likelyhod at all yet . CROMWEL,II,196.078.933

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_078:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
he woll sende thither prively a barke to knowe assuredly the truth
thereof . CROMWEL,II,196.078.934

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_078:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Many bruytes Rumours and Reportes be made aswell in and from Flaundres
as in and from some other parties . CROMWEL,II,196.078.935

the groundes thereof being vnexpressed and all thinges well wayed not
like to be suche indede as is reported . CROMWEL,II,196.078.936

take a phantazie indede that their suspicions be true
CROMWEL,II,196.078.937

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

CROMWEL,II,196.078.938

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

Other merking the wordes of the Inconstant and fyckel people bablyng
abrode thinke the same can not be so moche in the peoples mouth
withoute some ground as smoke is not withoute fyre .
CROMWEL,II,196.078.939

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

But for all this somtyme suche thinges do vanyshe awaye as the wynde .
CROMWEL,II,196.078.940

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_078:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Yet nevertheles I can not But <paren> like as your grace . of a
merveyllouse high wisedom for more assurance in all chaunces and
occurrentes maketh prouision in tyme for defense . </paren> so to
thinke that your grace woll not be further moved or pricked by suche
reportes or letteres vpon suche vnknowen reportes suspicions and tales
grounded than the thinges doo appere CROMWEL,II,196.078.941

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

shal never be quiete in mynd . CROMWEL,II,196.078.943

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

Thies I do not write as thinking your grace nedeth any warnyng thereof
being of so highe and excellent witt prudence and long experience . But
that I wold declare vnto your maiestie howe I doo for my part take the
thinges and as I thinke other men shuld tak $them {TEXT:then} {ED:SIC}
. And that no more celerite or precipitacion of thinges shuld be vsed
then of congruencye CROMWEL,II,196.078.944

shal prevaile thorough his grace Assuredly seing that nowe I
vndrestande from Irland that your rebelles Desmond Byryn O nelle and O
donelle do moche combyne and practise togeder , CROMWEL,II,197.078.945

Therfore wheras heretofore I have writen vnto your Maiesties depute at
Calais vnder the colour of good chere and entretenement to kepe the
said Chappuy there or elles if he wold not suffer to be so steyed by
colour of faire entretenement tyll Mr. Wryothesley shuld retourne that
then he shuld saye vnto him that for a special restraincte made afor
the date of his passport , he dereth not suffre him to passe tyll Mr.
Wryothesley be come or tyll he shuld further knowe your highnes
pleasure vpon that special point requiring hym to take pacience . I
beseche your Maieste to declare your owne pleasure and in cace the same
$shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} that he may also departe from Calais that then
it may please your highnes to sende my letteres herewith to my lorde
deputie theffect whereof is to contremand the former letteres and that
in nowise he shal steye the said Chappuys . whether the said
Wryothesley be arryved or no . CROMWEL,II,198.078.963

the waye of Flaunders of sundry dates as the xvi=th= and xviii=th= of

{ED:305._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:Apr._16_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please it your most excellent highnes , My very bounden duetie
remembred to your most noble Royall maieste , to vnderstand That even
nowe I have receyved newes from the man of Antwerp which your highnes
wote of writen in broken English of the Date of xj of Aprill , present
moneth . Theffect whereof is That in Germayn the Christen princes
assembled have as yet no answere from Themperour .
CROMWEL,II,211.081.997

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
but they loke dayly for it and also for the conclusion of all the
practike CROMWEL,II,211.081.998

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The said man writeth the said xj of Aprill he receyved letteres of the
xxiiij=th= of Marche from Toledo in Spayne by the which he
vnderstandeth , that thexchaunge of CLm=l= crones made by the Fowlkers
and Welsers to be paid in Augstburg within ij monethes shal serve for
to assemble fotemen to be conduced to Geanes for to go with Themperours
shippes which he hathe vndoubtedly prepared for Barbaria
CROMWEL,II,211.081.999

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But forbicause Themperesse is veray sicke and with chyld and her tyme
to be brought to bedd within ij or iij monethes vntyll suche tyme as
she be well Themperour doth not thinke to departe oute of Spayn
Wherfore he Jugeth that the Englishemen ought not to feare any thing
the flete of Themperour CROMWEL,II,211.081.1000

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
For they be all ordeyned for Barbaria as he saieth he hathe ever writen
. CROMWEL,II,211.081.1001

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
He thinketh that thadmyral of the lowe countreye is nowe vpon the see
with all the flete for spayn CROMWEL,II,211.081.1002

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and his person shal passe no further but retourne agayn to the lowe
contreyes by land CROMWEL,II,211.081.1003

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Englishemen may assuredly make their rekenyng that Themperour hathe
cause to think elleswhere then vpon them . CROMWEL,II,211.081.1004

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And for the verification and proue hereof as he allegeth to have writen
heretofore . Themperour hathe not consented to the popes desires nor
that his Mandementes shuld be published neyther in Spayn neyther in any
other his dominions . That englishemen shuld be destroyed both bodyes
and goodes wheresoever they could be found As that pope wold they
<P_II,212> shuld be which desires although he calleth them Sanctissimo
yet we ought to repute tyrannissimo CROMWEL,II,212.081.1005

RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48

and so the world ought to Juge seen that he procedeth without reason .

RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48

of thise persones is well knowen as it may be better consydered then
told . CROMWEL,II,212.081.1013

RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But sythens that in diuerse parties there is conformable talking of it
I thinke therupon CROMWEL,II,212.081.1016

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_081:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and it semeth vnto me to be of good lykelyhod That the oone of the
felowes that is ever gladd to hold and kepe in hand is for to sett the
other in some snare or tanglyng , and that he doth for the same geve
him faire wordes to feade him with Albeit he hath no mynde to come to
theffect And that if he shuld come to it peradventure he thinketh to
leave him in the daunce and Revolve himself to some other place . By
the which way the other shuld remayne quyte of such thinges as be
demaunded of him or the felowe shuld lese some steye of freendes if he
have any with danger to make banke rota , which shuld be more pleasure
to the other then to see his encreasse CROMWEL,II,212.081.1017

{ED:306._CROMWELL_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT.}

{ED:Apr._16_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_082:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Mr Wyat after my right herty commendations to you forasmuch as the
kinges maiestie hath muche hert to know what is the mater that ye can
not write but declare by mouth , Therfore his grace willeth ye shall
with all possible diligence returne , CROMWEL,II,213.082.1032

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_082:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and in cace ye can not so sone com the kinges maiestes will is that ye
shal make the shortiest abode there ye can , and in the meane tyme
because of your better accointaunce ye shall inquire what themperour
woll this yere or-5 go out of spayne or where icaaenst the turkye , or
barbarowse and how all stondyth bytwene fraunce and themperour and news
ther CROMWEL,II,213.082.1033

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
LETTER:CROMWEL_082:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Thus bicause this berer can Infourme you of the newes . I shal withoute
longer Recitaill committe you to almyghty god . CROMWEL,II,213.082.1034

{ED:307._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:Apr._19_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My most humble and bounden Duetie remembred to your excellent maiestie
It may please the same to be aduertised that as this present daye I had
not failed to sett foreward and prepared that as tomorrowe I myght have
wayted and geven my due and promissed attendaunce vpon your highnes ,
but that I fynde vpon me some grutge of an ague and thinke that
withstanding the first bruntes by the sparing of oone or two dayes I
$shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} the better hable to contynue my duetie of
seruice towardes your grace many monethes and yeres ,
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1038

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and yet in the meane tyme I shal not be ydell CROMWEL,II,214.083.1039

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
but Intende to your maiesties seruice as I have done hitherto , and
shall as long as god shal geve me breth and power to styrr .
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1040

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I have sithens my last Letteres Receyved aduertisementes from your
graces oratour in Flaundres Stephan Vaughan a grete part wherof your
highnes hath had alredy , part of them as thadvise of the bishop
Lundensis Themperours ambassadour in Frankford .
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1041

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
We hard not afore CROMWEL,II,214.083.1042

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
but seen they advise to take such waye as his Jugement is they shuld
doo so I thinke bicause it shal not be easy to them to compasse their
purpose that at the last their entreprises shal come to nothing ,
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1043

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and so in space shal appere goddes grace . CROMWEL,II,214.083.1044

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
In your letteres by the said Vaughan writen to your Maieste the matiers
may be seen more at large , CROMWEL,II,214.083.1045

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and for that purpose I have Joyned them herewith Vpon the letteres sent
vnto me by your highnes most honorable counseill .
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1046

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The marquise hath bene examyned , CROMWEL,II,214.083.1047

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and In effect , albeit she pretendeth Ignorance and no knowlege of the
person that shuld reporte the tale , yet neuertheles she confesseth in
substance , the moche like wordes to have ben told her .
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1048

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I shall assaye to the vttermost of my power , and never cesse tyll the
botom of her stomacke may be clerely opened and disclosed ,
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1049

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and to that shal I not be slack , to thintent that If I may pycke oute
the same and be as helthy as I trust to make meself , I shall on
mondaye next by mouth declare the same vnto your highnes more then I
could by any writing . CROMWEL,II,214.083.1050

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I trust allmyghty god shall bringe all thinges to lyght that any
vngodly and vntrue persons have conspired agenste your grace as
hitherto <paren> praysed by god </paren> it hath ben seen .
CROMWEL,II,214.083.1051

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The ernest and true examynation of Leynham sheweth that of a long
season he hath bene a madd prophete CROMWEL,II,214.083.1052

RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_083:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I have receyved letteres from my lord of Norffolk which I sende herwith
to thentent that your highnes may knowe howe grevousely his lordship
taketh the assignement I have made to Anthony Rouse of oone of Sir
Edward Ichinghams doughters . who by all the very true aduertisementes
that I can have is your Maiesties warde and to your graces vse
appoincted to the custodye of the said Rouse CROMWEL,II,215.083.1064

CROMWEL,II,215.083.1065

RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48

matier , weye also therwith , My said Lorde the duke of Norffolkes good
merites and determyne the best in that mater to be fulfylled and
accomplished accordingly . CROMWEL,II,215.083.1066

{ED:309._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:[Apr._23,_1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My most bounden duetie of reuerence and honour to your maieste right
humbly remembred It may like the same to wite that to my grete regret
sorowe and displeasour by reason of certain accesse of a fever tertian
that is com vpon me I am compelled to be nowe absent and to forbeare
such myn attendaunce vpon your Royall highnes as sundry wayes I am
bounde vnto and as I purposed yesterdaye in the mornyng and made meself
redy to have don whan my fytt of the ague casted me downe and held me
in a grete hete aboute a x howres , CROMWEL,II,216.085.1079

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
the payne of the disease greveth me nothing so moch as that doth that I
$can $not {TEXT:cannot} be as I shuld there present and employe my
power to your graces affaires and seruice as my hert desyreth to do
CROMWEL,II,216.085.1080

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
but I trust so to withstande myn ennemy the fever in the very begynning
and eere ever it shal have more hold vpon me that I trust shortely to
ouercome it . CROMWEL,II,216.085.1081

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
In the meane tyme , I doubte not but your bonteouse and benigne grace
of his accoustumed clemency woll hold me for excused ,
CROMWEL,II,216.085.1082

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and thereof I beseche your Maieste most humbly .
CROMWEL,II,216.085.1083

LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

Sadleyer the which I thought to have brought meself and have knowen
your graciouse pleasure therupon . CROMWEL,II,216.085.1084

why and to what purpose the exchange of the CLM=l=. d=os= shuld be made

that is howe the hulkes were contremanded to retourn back The sending
of Andelo , in post to the bishop of Rome to Andreas de Auria , to the
$veniciens and to retourn within xlv days . That themperour purposeth
to come in to flandres , and that the Frenshe king wold have him to
passe thorough his Realme but he entendeth not so to do and therfore it
is thought that Andelo is sent to make his excuses , And suche other
poinctes which your grace is alredy aduertised of .

LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Monsieur de Marrillac the Frenshe kinges ambassadour sent me worde that
he had some newes not of grete importance to make me participant of ,
requiring to knowe whan I myght have leasure to heare him wherupon
seing meself in myn accesse of fever I sent Solemont vnto hym desyring
hym to <P_II,218> have me excused , and no lesse to declare vnto hym
than he wold to meself . CROMWEL,II,218.085.1098

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
His declaracion was that by the letteres of Monsieur de Rangon and by
other aduertisementes he had advise that assuredly the Turke made
merveillouse preparacions both by see and by land to Invade Christendom
, and that alredy he had sent a grete Armye towardes Castro nouo which
the Veneciens toke from him to recover it If he can . And that the
Sophy King of Perse had an oratour with the Turke .
CROMWEL,II,218.085.1099

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And Interroged by the said Soulemont whither the said Turke wold
converte his forces he answered that he was extremely sett and bent
agenst the Veneciens and that he was vtterly determyned to extincte
them , and to put them to the worst aslong as he shal have any power .
And that of peace or trewes he shuld never take noone with the said
Veneciens . that Grittj of Venise was in Turky in dede but he pretended
not to be as Oratour of the Veneciens but as a sutour to have certain
goodes which George Grittj his brother <paren> who died in turkye
</paren> had left vnto him at the tyme of his decesse , but that
nevertheles If he shuld have perceyved opportunite the Veneciens had
geven him charge to move the Turke of some argument but there was no
suche oportune occasion as the said Marrillac said . And that also the
Veneciens were never put in hope of agrement with the Turk but onely by
some of the Bassas , for coveytise of suche presentes as the Veneciens
, and other be accoustumed to geve them whan they go in ambassade . And
that for the said avariciouse coveytyse the said Bassas had often tymes
prayed the said Marrillac , to byde the Veneciens , to sende som
ambassadours , which he refused to do . CROMWEL,II,218.085.1100

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_085:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But ones he shewed the same to the Turke himself who answered to him
that if the Bassas shuld any more attempte such matiers they shuld dye
for it and that he shuld never have peace with the Veneciens affirmyng
the same by the solemne othes of his Turkishe lawe
CROMWEL,II,218.085.1101

<P_II,219>

{ED:310._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:Apr._24_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please it your most noble maieste , after my very bounden duetie right
humbly remembred with most herty and affectuouse thankes for your
graciouse benignite extended vpon me Infinite wayes and nowe in
speciall for your facil acceptacion of myn absence , and confortable
graciouse wordes , to vnderstand that yesterdaye aboute none arryved
vnto me hither your Maiestes seruauntes M=r= Christophor Mount and Mr.
Paynell . And shewed vnto me that the Duke of Saxony hath sent hither
to your highnes his vicechauncelour Burgart and the Landisgrave , a
gentilman of his , of good experience that can speke sundry langages
and hath ben often tymes sent to sundry princes in missage as he is
nowe to your grace CROMWEL,II,219.086.1118

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
At their departure from Frankford the assemble was not as yet dissolued
nor full conclusion taken therupon . Albeit some thought that it wold
com to the point <P_II,220> of an abstinence of any molestacion on both
parties for xviij monethes or soo . CROMWEL,II,220.086.1119

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The said Burgart and his collega with iiij other persones in their
company arrived hither also yesterdaye CROMWEL,II,220.086.1120

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and were brought by the said Christophor to Jennyns sergeant of your
graces pasterye house there to remayne for such tyme , tyll they may be
otherwise better provided of an other loging . CROMWEL,II,220.086.1121

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I have not as yet for myn indisposition spoken with them .
CROMWEL,II,220.086.1122

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But by your graces seruaunt I can perceyve that the Landisgrave and
Duke also do contynue styll in their loving and frendely obseruacion
towardes your maieste , very Joyouse of your graces allyance and
confederacion If it shal please your highnes to entre with them ,
CROMWEL,II,220.086.1123

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and so concernyng thesame poinct their oratours be sent hither at this
tyme CROMWEL,II,220.086.1124

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But what their Instructions do beare your graces seruauntes be not made
pryve of . Howe be it they thinke that they woll require concordie in
doctrine , and mutuel helpe of defense in cace of Invasion with
Indifferent condicions of Reciproke . CROMWEL,II,220.086.1125

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as for the first point the said Landgrave hath found that part of
your graces proclamacions somwhat strange wherin it is spoken de
coniugio sacerdotum , sayeng that thesame was agenst the true doctrine
of the votes which they professed CROMWEL,II,220.086.1126

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and herupon also Melanchthon hath writen vnto me that he hath seen that
proclamacion wherin certain evill doctrines be forbeden , and also
certain true doctrine whiche they professe in Alemayn concernyng de
votis et coniugio , but that he hopeth forasmoch as in the said
proclamacions your highnes promisseth to abolishe abuses that your
grace shal consydere thesame more exactely and at the last mitigate
thesame . CROMWEL,II,220.086.1127

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
They have as Mr. Christophor sayeth , ben ernestly in hand with him for
thesame poinct , who answered that although he knewe not your graces
consyderacions in that behalf , yet he might well affirme that your
highnes is not to scrupulouse in the matier de votis and that sundry
nonnes and religiouse women have ben discharged oute of their houses
with honest pensions during their lyves and not forbeden but suffred to
marye . CROMWEL,II,220.086.1128

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But as for prestes he thinketh the cause of the prohibicion was bicause
they must preach the worde of god and that it is thought that the
common people as yet weake in the knowlege of the worde and of other
thinges myght therby conceyve an opinion of concupiscence in them , and
by reason thereof contempne their preachinges and the worde of god
CROMWEL,II,220.086.1129

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:CROMWEL_086:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But what your grace wold do after ward whan the people shall wexe
stronger and hable to eate solide meate , he answered he could not
diffine nor Juge , but that he doubted not but your grace did nothing
without good cause and reason and with grete consyderacion , <P_II,221>
with the which answer the said landgrave and other were merveillousely
satisfied So that as it is to be thought they woll not moche sticke to
that pointe CROMWEL,II,221.086.1130

by thies wordes , Multj vbique hoc tempore astute cogitatis
Interpretationibus excusant abusus aut leniunt , vt arte stabiliant eos
sicut fit in libro Colonie edito cuj titulus est Enchiridion , hanc
sophisticam perniciosam ecclesie video Imitarj Mitratos apud vos Sed
cavendum est ne hac sophistica rursus obruatur veritas Nam ad
tranquilitatem durabilem etiam simplex veritas vtilior est .

{TEXT:shalbe} duely here examyned vppon suche pointes as be deposed

that I never tooke you to be a man of suche sorte .

desired thenne I shall neade nowe to recounte and expresse .

in perpetuel prisonne during lief adding that you woll soo write in
that cace to the Kinges Maieste . CROMWEL,II,225.087.1156

other could not have the patience to suffre the punishment thereof to
be made by your Lordship and other of the counseill withoute hote
proceding in his fume to Revenge hym self And to geve hym a blowe as it
appereth by Witnesses he did . CROMWEL,II,228.088.1167

counseill , So ye shal vpon suche other matiers of smale Importance
assemble your heddes to gether and Charitably withoute any particular
affection proceding rather to heale and cure the membres deseased or
corrupt then to cutt them awaye without any necessite , to see suche a
gentil and Indifferent ordre taken in thinges as may be for the quiete

{ED:316._CROMWELL_TO_BONNER.}

{ED:July_24,_1539.}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_089:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My lorde after my right hertie and most affectuouse commendacions Your
Lordshipp shal vnderstande that yesterday confereunt had vpon the
matters of Monsieur de la Rochipot betwene the frenche ambassadour and
Monsieur de Dampont on of the frenche kinges gentilmen on the on partie
and certeyne of the Stylyard and their counsaill with Doctour Layton
Oliuer Leight Hughs Ryvet and other one the other pertie , wherby it
appeared that without the wrounge of the Osterlinges and great
preiudice of the kinges Jurisdicion and <P_II,231> evill example and
consequent in tymes comming his maieste coulde not Renvoye the mater to
be decided in Fraunce Nor admitt declinatoriam feri quam gallus
proponebat . CROMWEL,II,231.089.1183

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:39?
LETTER:CROMWEL_089:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And althouight the said ambassadour and Dampont haue heard the motives
and reasons therof , yet neuertheles his highnes not trusting hollye to
their declaracion and Rapport hathe remitted the same to be declared
aswell by you as by them , to the Frenche Kinge , as it appearethe by
his graces Letteres , the copie wherof ye shall receyve herwith .

$been handled favourablie , and with diligence sethe their comminge .
Furst ye shall vnderstande that after the recept of the Frenche kinges
, Letteres Soulemount was sent to the ambassadors for to know their
reasons and allegacions wherby they entende to move the kinges highnes
to revoke the sentence , at whiche tyme they , as vnprovided or not
fully instructed gave him for that tyme a slander answer , whervpon the
Sonday after which was the ix=th= of July , The stilliardes with ther
counseill were sent thether to the Ambassadour to shew vnto him their
reasons and the Justice of the sentence . And to answer vnto suche
reasons as the Frenchemen wold allege . CROMWEL,II,231.089.1185

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

moste honorable counsell they shuld put all theyr reasons and
allegacions with their factes in writinge and delyuer them to the said
Solymon CROMWEL,II,231.089.1186

{ED:322._CROMWELL_TO_LORD_LISLE.}

{ED:Oct._18_[1539].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_090:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
After my righte hartie commendacions to your Lordship Thise $shall $be
{TEXT:shalbe} taduertise you that for certain purposes the specialties
wherof you shal further knowe herafter The kinges Maiestes pleasure is
that you shal vieu his graces howse there called Thexchequier that with
all diligence all thinges therin necessarie to be amendyd may be
indelayedly repayryd , For the whiche purpose I haue by his graces
commaundement writen also to his highnes surveyour there , who by your
advise shall sett in hande withe the same . CROMWEL,II,237.090.1212

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
RECIPIENT:ARTHUR_LISLE:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:CROMWEL_090:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Furthermore his Maieste woolde that you shuld cause the stretes and
Lanes there to be vieued for the pavementes and where any defaulte is
to give commaundement to those whiche shulde repayre the same to see it
immediatly amended , endevoring yourselfes to put all other thinges
within the said towne in the most honest and clenely ordre you canne
devise Wherein you shall administre to his Maieste very thankfull
pleasure CROMWEL,II,237.090.1213

LETTER:CROMWEL_092:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Moste gracyous King and most mercyfull souerayng your most humble most
obbeysand and most bounden subiett and most lamentable seruaunt and
prysoner prostrate at the Feate of your most excellent magestye haue
herd your pleasure by the mouthe of your Comptroller which was that I
sholde wrytte to your most excellent highnes such thinges as I thought
mete to be wryttyn Consernyng my most myserable State and Condicyon for
the whiche your most haboundaunt goodnes benignyte and lycens the
Immortalle god three and On rewarde your magestye ,

For lycens for the departure of the strang maydens I then requeryd them

Comyttyd the Secret matyer vnto me onlye of purpose that She myght haue
bene Inducyd to suche pleasaunt and honorable Fassyons as might haue
beene to your gracys comfforde which aboue all thinges as god knowyth I
dyd most Couyt and desyre but that I openyd my mowthe to any Creature
after your Majestye commytted the Secresye therof to me Other then
onlye to my lorde admyrall which I dyde by your gracys comandement
which was vppon Sondaye last in the mornyng whom I then Founde as
willing and glade to seke remydye For your Comffort and consolacyon
CROMWEL,II,266.092.1267

<P_II,268>

{ED:349._CROMWELL_TO_HENRY_VIII.}

{ED:June_30_[1540].}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:CROMWEL_093:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Most mercyfull king and most gracyous souerayng lorde may hit please
the same to be aduertysyd that the laste tyme it pleasyd your bening
goodnes , to send vnto me the right honourable lorde Chaunceler the
Right honorable Duke of Norffoke and the lord admyrall to examyne and
also to declare to me dyuers thinges from yowr magestye amongist the
which one specyall thing they movyd and thervppon chargyd me as I
woolde answer , beffor god at the dredffull daye of Judgement and also
vppon the extreme daunger and Dampnacyon of my sowlle and consyens to
saye what I knew in the mariage and consernyng the mariage betwene your
highnes and the quene to the which I answeryd as I knew declaring to
them the partyculers as nyghe as I then coulde call to Remembraunce
which when they hadde harde they in {TEXT:in} {ED:SIC} your maiestees
name and vppon lyke charge as thay hadde gyvyn me beffore commaundyd me
to wrytt to your highnes the trewthe as moch as I knew in that matyer ,
which now I doo , and the veraye trewth as god shall salve me , to the
vttermost of my knowlage . CROMWEL,II,268.093.1286

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:CROMWEL_093:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Fyrst after your maiestye herde of the ladye Anne of Clevys arryvall at
dover and that her Jerneyes wer appoyntyd towardes grenwiche and that
She sholde be at Rochester on new yeres evyn at nyght your highnes
declaryd to me that ye woolde pryvelye vysyt her at Rochester vppon
newyeres daye adding thes woordes to norishe loue , which accordinglye
your grace dide vppon new yeres daye as is abouesayd ,
CROMWEL,II,268.093.1287

and the next day being Frydaye your grace reternyd to grenwyche wher I
spake with your grace and demandyd of your magestye how ye lykyd the
ladye Anne CROMWEL,II,268.093.1288

your highnes answeryd as me thought hevelye And not plesantlye nothing
so well as She was spokyn of Saying Ferther that yf your highnes hadde
known asmoche beffore as ye then knew she shold not haue Commen within
this Realme , Saying as by way of lamentacyon what remedye , vnto the
which I answeryd and said I knew none but was veraye Sory therffore
CROMWEL,II,268.093.1289

selffe , to Commone of thos matyers , and to know what commyssyon the
Agenttes of Clevys hadde browght as well touching the perfformaunce of
the Conuenaunttes sent beffore from hens to Doctour Wotton to haue bene
Concludyd in Clevys , as also in the declaracyon how the matyers ,
stode for the Conuenauntts of Maryage betwene the Duke of loreyns Son
and the sayd ladye Anne , whervppon Osleger and Hogeston wer Callyd and
the matyers purpossyd , wherby it playnlye apperyd that they were moche
astonyed and abasshed and desyryd that $they might make answer in the
next mornyng which was sondaye CROMWEL,II,269.093.1298

and ther eftsons was purposyd vnto them aswell touching the Comyssyon
For the performaunce of the tretye and artycles Sent to maister Wotton
as also touching the Contractes and Couenaunttes of mariage betwene the
Duke of lorayns Son , and the ladye Anne and what termes thay stodde in
, To the whiche thinges so purposyd thay answeryd as men moche
perplexyd that as touching Commyssyon thay hadde none to trete
CROMWEL,II,269.093.1300

was made , and that thay were but spowsaylles , CROMWEL,II,269.093.1301

AUTHOR:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?

Clevys the Fyrst Artycles Ratyffyed vnder the Duke thayr maisters Signe
and Seale , and also the copye of the reuocacyon made betwene the Duke
of lorayns Son and the ladye Anne , vppon the which answers I was sent
to your highnes by my lordes of your said Counsayle to declare to your
highnes what answere they hadde made and Came to your highnes by the
prevey wey into your prevey Chambre and Declaryd to the same all the
Cyrcumstaunces wherwith your grace was veray <P_II,270> moch displeasyd
Saying I am not well handelyd , insomoche that I mought well persayue
that your highnes was Fully determenyd not to haue goone thorow with
the maryage at that tyme Saying vnto me thes woordes or the lyke in
effect that yf it were not that she is com So Farre into my realme and
the great preparacyons that my states & people hathe made For her and
For Fere of makyng of a Ruffull in the woorlde that is to meane to
dryve her brother into the handes of the emperowre and Frenche kynges
handes being now to gether I woolde neuer haue ne marye her , so that I
myght well persayve your grace was neyther Content with the person ne
yet content with the proceding of the Agenttes ,
CROMWEL,II,270.093.1302
